<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1236090951">.mw-parser-output .hatnote{font-style:italic}.mw-parser-output div.hatnote{padding-left:1.6em;margin-bottom:0.5em}.mw-parser-output .hatnote i{font-style:normal}.mw-parser-output .hatnote+link+.hatnote{margin-top:-0.5em}@media print{body.ns-0 .mw-parser-output .hatnote{display:none!important}}</style><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">This article is about the Australian sporting organisation. For the sport itself, see <a href="/wiki/Australian_rules_football" title="Australian rules football">Australian rules football</a>. For the women's league, see <a href="/wiki/AFL_Women%27s" title="AFL Women&#39;s">AFL Women's</a>. For the Australian national men’s soccer league, see <a href="/wiki/A-League_Men" title="A-League Men">A-League Men</a>.</div>

nowrap">International cup(s)</th><td class="infobox-data"><a href="/wiki/Australian_Football_International_Cup" title="Australian Football International Cup">Australian Football International Cup</a></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label" style="white-space: nowrap">Official website</th><td class="infobox-data"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.afl.com.au/">afl.com.au</a></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>The <b>Australian Football League</b> (<b>AFL</b>) is the pre-eminent <a href="/wiki/Professional_sports" title="Professional sports">professional</a> competition of <a href="/wiki/Australian_rules_football" title="Australian rules football">Australian rules football</a>. It was originally named the Victorian Football League (VFL) and was founded in 1896 as a breakaway competition from the <a href="/wiki/Victorian_Football_League#Victorian_Football_Association" title="Victorian Football League">Victorian Football Association</a> (VFA), with its <a href="/wiki/1897_VFL_season" title="1897 VFL season">inaugural season</a> in 1897. It changed its name to Australian Football League in 1990 after expanding its competition to other Australian states in the 1980s. The AFL publishes its <i><a href="/wiki/Laws_of_Australian_football" class="mw-redirect" title="Laws of Australian football">Laws of Australian football</a></i>, which are used, with variations, by other Australian rules football organisations.
</p><p>The AFL competition currently consists of 18 teams spread over Australia's five mainland states, with <a href="/wiki/Tasmania_Football_Club" title="Tasmania Football Club">Tasmania</a> to join the league as its 19th team in 2028.<sup id="cite_ref-19thteam-ABC_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19thteam-ABC-4"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>4<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> AFL premiership season matches have been played in all states and mainland territories, as well as in New Zealand and China to expand its audience.
</p><p>The AFL premiership season currently consists of a 23-match regular (or home-and-away) season, which runs from March to September. The team with the best record at the end of the home-and-away season is awarded the <a href="/wiki/List_of_VFL/AFL_minor_premiers" title="List of VFL/AFL minor premiers">minor premiership</a>; the top eight teams then play off in a four-round <a href="/wiki/AFL_finals_series" title="AFL finals series">finals series</a>, culminating in the <a href="/wiki/AFL_Grand_Final" title="AFL Grand Final">AFL Grand Final</a>, which is normally held at the <a href="/wiki/Melbourne_Cricket_Ground" title="Melbourne Cricket Ground">Melbourne Cricket Ground</a> each year. The grand final winners are termed the <a href="/wiki/List_of_VFL/AFL_premiers" title="List of VFL/AFL premiers">premiers</a>, the most important team prizes for which are the premiership cup and <a href="/wiki/Pennant_(sports)" title="Pennant (sports)">flag</a>. <a href="/wiki/Carlton_Football_Club" title="Carlton Football Club">Carlton</a>, <a href="/wiki/Collingwood_Football_Club" title="Collingwood Football Club">Collingwood</a> and <a href="/wiki/Essendon_Football_Club" title="Essendon Football Club">Essendon</a> are the joint-most successful clubs in the competition, having each won 16 premierships. The <a href="/wiki/Brisbane_Lions" title="Brisbane Lions">Brisbane Lions</a> are the reigning premiers, having won the <a href="/wiki/2024_AFL_Grand_Final" title="2024 AFL Grand Final">2024 AFL Grand Final</a>.
</p>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r886046785">.mw-parser-output .toclimit-2 .toclevel-1 ul,.mw-parser-output .toclimit-3 .toclevel-2 ul,.mw-parser-output .toclimit-4 .toclevel-3 ul,.mw-parser-output .toclimit-5 .toclevel-4 ul,.mw-parser-output .toclimit-6 .toclevel-5 ul,.mw-parser-output .toclimit-7 .toclevel-6 ul{display:none}</style><div class="toclimit-4"><meta property="mw:PageProp/toc" /></div>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="History">History</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Australian_Football_League&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Australian_Football_League" title="History of the Australian Football League">History of the Australian Football League</a></div>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="VFL_era_(1897–1989)"><span id="VFL_era_.281897.E2.80.931989.29"></span>VFL era (1897–1989)</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Australian_Football_League&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: VFL era (1897–1989)"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="Background_and_founding">Background and founding</h4><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Australian_Football_League&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Background and founding"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:1896_VFA_premiership_list.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/1896_VFA_premiership_list.jpg/250px-1896_VFA_premiership_list.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="235" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/1896_VFA_premiership_list.jpg/330px-1896_VFA_premiership_list.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/7/7d/1896_VFA_premiership_list.jpg 2x" data-file-width="421" data-file-height="449" /></a><figcaption>The final standing of the 1896 VFA ladder. <a href="/wiki/Collingwood_Football_Club" title="Collingwood Football Club">Collingwood</a>, <a href="/wiki/Essendon_Football_Club" title="Essendon Football Club">Essendon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fitzroy_Football_Club" title="Fitzroy Football Club">Fitzroy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Geelong_Football_Club" title="Geelong Football Club">Geelong</a>, <a href="/wiki/Melbourne_Football_Club" title="Melbourne Football Club">Melbourne</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sydney_Swans" title="Sydney Swans">South Melbourne</a>, <a href="/wiki/Carlton_Football_Club" title="Carlton Football Club">Carlton</a> and <a href="/wiki/St_Kilda_Football_Club" title="St Kilda Football Club">St Kilda</a> would form the VFL the following year.</figcaption></figure>
<p>Several of the AFL's current member clubs date back to the origins of <a href="/wiki/Australian_rules_football" title="Australian rules football">Australian football</a> and were instrumental in establishing the sport's popularity and the AFL. The oldest club is <a href="/wiki/Melbourne_Football_Club" title="Melbourne Football Club">Melbourne Football Club</a>, which wrote the first laws of the code, and <a href="/wiki/Geelong_Football_Club" title="Geelong Football Club">Geelong</a>, which date back to 1858 and 1859 respectively, while <a href="/wiki/Melbourne_University_Football_Club" title="Melbourne University Football Club">Melbourne University</a>, also founded in 1859, is also one of the oldest clubs to have later participated in the competition.
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Victorian_Football_Association" class="mw-redirect" title="Victorian Football Association">Victorian Football Association</a> (VFA) was established in 1877 and quickly went on to become <a href="/wiki/Victoria_(Australia)" class="mw-redirect" title="Victoria (Australia)">Victoria</a>'s football competition. During the 1890s, an off-field power struggle occurred between the VFA's stronger and weaker clubs, the former seeking greater administrative control commensurate with their relative financial contribution to the game. This came to a head in 1896 when it was proposed that gate profits, which were always lower in matches involving the weaker clubs, be shared equally among all teams in the VFA. After it was intimated that the proposal would be put to a vote, six of the strongest clubs—<a href="/wiki/Collingwood_Football_Club" title="Collingwood Football Club">Collingwood</a>, <a href="/wiki/Essendon_Football_Club" title="Essendon Football Club">Essendon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fitzroy_Football_Club" title="Fitzroy Football Club">Fitzroy</a>, Geelong, Melbourne and <a href="/wiki/Sydney_Swans" title="Sydney Swans">South Melbourne</a>—seceded from the VFA and later invited <a href="/wiki/Carlton_Football_Club" title="Carlton Football Club">Carlton</a> and <a href="/wiki/St_Kilda_Football_Club" title="St Kilda Football Club">St Kilda</a> to join them in founding a new competition, the Victorian Football League (VFL). The remaining VFA clubs—<a href="/wiki/Footscray_Football_Club" class="mw-redirect" title="Footscray Football Club">Footscray</a>, <a href="/wiki/North_Melbourne_Football_Club" title="North Melbourne Football Club">North Melbourne</a>, <a href="/wiki/Port_Melbourne_Football_Club" title="Port Melbourne Football Club">Port Melbourne</a>, <a href="/wiki/Richmond_Football_Club" title="Richmond Football Club">Richmond</a> and <a href="/wiki/Williamstown_Football_Club" title="Williamstown Football Club">Williamstown</a>—were given the opportunity to compete as junior sides at a level beneath the VFL but rejected the offer and remained for the <a href="/wiki/1897_VFA_season" title="1897 VFA season">1897 VFA season</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-secession2_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-secession2-5"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>5<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="1897–1900s:_Inaugural_VFL_season_and_early_years"><span id="1897.E2.80.931900s:_Inaugural_VFL_season_and_early_years"></span>1897–1900s: Inaugural VFL season and early years</h4><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Australian_Football_League&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: 1897–1900s: Inaugural VFL season and early years"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-left" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Essendon_fc_1897.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Essendon_fc_1897.jpg/250px-Essendon_fc_1897.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="167" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Essendon_fc_1897.jpg/330px-Essendon_fc_1897.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Essendon_fc_1897.jpg/500px-Essendon_fc_1897.jpg 2x" data-file-width="620" data-file-height="470" /></a><figcaption><a href="/wiki/Essendon_Football_Club" title="Essendon Football Club">Essendon</a> won the inaugural VFL premiership by finishing on top of the <a href="/wiki/1897_VFL_finals_series" title="1897 VFL finals series">1897 round robin finals ladder</a>. A new finals system was implemented during the <a href="/wiki/1898_VFL_season" title="1898 VFL season">1898 VFL season</a> in order that a final match, or "grand final", should determine the premiers.</figcaption></figure>
<p>The VFL's inaugural season occurred in 1897. It made several innovations early on to entice the public's interest, including an annual <a href="/wiki/Playoffs" title="Playoffs">finals</a> tournament, rather than awarding the premiership to the team with the best record through the season; and, the formal establishment of the modern scoring system, in which six points are awarded for a goal and one point for a behind.
</p><p>Although the VFL and the VFA continued to compete for spectator interest for many years, the VFL quickly established itself as the premier competition in Victoria. In 1908, the league expanded to ten teams, with <a href="/wiki/Richmond_Football_Club" title="Richmond Football Club">Richmond</a> crossing from the VFA and <a href="/wiki/University_Football_Club" class="mw-redirect" title="University Football Club">University Football Club</a> from the <a href="/wiki/Victorian_Amateur_Football_Association" title="Victorian Amateur Football Association">Metropolitan Junior Football Association</a>. Professionalism began from the 1911 season, with clubs permitted to pay players beyond the reimbursement of expenses for the first time.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>6<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> University, after three promising seasons, finished last each year from 1911 until 1914, including losing 51 matches in a row, in part caused by its players' focus on their studies rather than football and in part because it had chosen to remain amateur; as a result, the club withdrew from the VFL at the end of 1914.<sup id="cite_ref-The_University_Team2_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_University_Team2-7"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>7<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceA2_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA2-8"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>8<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/List_of_VFA/VFL_premiers" title="List of VFA/VFL premiers">VFL premier</a> and the premier of the <a href="/wiki/SANFL" class="mw-redirect" title="SANFL">South Australian Football League</a> met in a playoff matches for the <a href="/wiki/Championship_of_Australia" title="Championship of Australia">Championship of Australia</a> beginning in <a href="/wiki/1888_Championship_of_Australia" title="1888 Championship of Australia">1888</a> with a 3-game playoff between South Melbourne from the VFL and the <a href="/wiki/Norwood_Football_Club" title="Norwood Football Club">Norwood</a> the most successful club in the SAFA. Matches where then held sporadically during the 1890s as single game playoffs and then annually from 1907 until 1914 (except 1912). South Australian clubs won 8 of the 11 Titles of which <a href="/wiki/Port_Adelaide_Football_Club" title="Port Adelaide Football Club">Port Adelaide</a> was the most successful winning four titles in 1890, 1910, 1913 and 1914. The majority of the matches were held in South Australia at <a href="/wiki/Adelaide_Oval" title="Adelaide Oval">Adelaide Oval</a>. Following the outbreak of World War 1 the Championship playoff ceased and wasn't revived until 1968.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="1915–1945:_Three_VFA_clubs_join_the_VFL"><span id="1915.E2.80.931945:_Three_VFA_clubs_join_the_VFL"></span>1915–1945: Three VFA clubs join the VFL</h4><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Australian_Football_League&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: 1915–1945: Three VFA clubs join the VFL"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/The_VFL_during_the_World_Wars" class="mw-redirect" title="The VFL during the World Wars">The VFL during the World Wars</a></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:1924_Victorian_Football_Championship.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/1924_Victorian_Football_Championship.jpg/250px-1924_Victorian_Football_Championship.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="153" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/1924_Victorian_Football_Championship.jpg/330px-1924_Victorian_Football_Championship.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/1924_Victorian_Football_Championship.jpg/500px-1924_Victorian_Football_Championship.jpg 2x" data-file-width="553" data-file-height="385" /></a><figcaption>In 1924, <a href="/wiki/Footscray_Football_Club" class="mw-redirect" title="Footscray Football Club">Footscray</a>, the premiers of the VFA, defeated Essendon, the VFL premiers, in the <a href="/wiki/1924_Championship_of_Victoria" title="1924 Championship of Victoria">Championship of Victoria</a>. The result played a large part in Footscray, Hawthorn and North Melbourne gaining entry into the VFL the following year.</figcaption></figure>
<p>In 1916, <a href="/wiki/Zoning_(Australian_rules_football)" title="Zoning (Australian rules football)">district football</a> was introduced, meaning new players from metropolitan Melbourne were allocated to clubs based on residential address.<sup id="cite_ref-QC_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-QC-9"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>9<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In 1925, the VFL expanded from nine teams to twelve, with <a href="/wiki/Footscray_Football_Club" class="mw-redirect" title="Footscray Football Club">Footscray</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hawthorn_Football_Club" title="Hawthorn Football Club">Hawthorn</a> and <a href="/wiki/North_Melbourne_Football_Club" title="North Melbourne Football Club">North Melbourne</a> each crossing from the VFA. North Melbourne and Hawthorn remained very weak in the VFL for a very long period. Although <a href="/wiki/North_Melbourne_Football_Club" title="North Melbourne Football Club">North Melbourne</a> would become the first of the 1925 expansion sides to reach a grand final in <a href="/wiki/1950_VFL_Grand_Final" class="mw-redirect" title="1950 VFL Grand Final">1950</a>, initially it was <a href="/wiki/Footscray_Football_Club" class="mw-redirect" title="Footscray Football Club">Footscray</a> that adapted to the VFL with the most ease of the three clubs and by 1928 were well off the bottom of the ladder.
</p><p>From 1927 to 1930, Collingwood became the first and only VFL team, to win four successive premierships.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="1946–1975:_Post-war_golden_years"><span id="1946.E2.80.931975:_Post-war_golden_years"></span>1946–1975: Post-war golden years</h4><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Australian_Football_League&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: 1946–1975: Post-war golden years"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>In 1952, the VFL hosted a national day, when all six matches were played outside Melbourne. Matches were played at the <a href="/wiki/Sydney_Cricket_Ground" title="Sydney Cricket Ground">Sydney Cricket Ground</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brisbane_Exhibition_Ground" class="mw-redirect" title="Brisbane Exhibition Ground">Brisbane Exhibition Ground</a>, <a href="/wiki/North_Hobart_Oval" title="North Hobart Oval">North Hobart Oval</a>, <a href="/wiki/Albury_Sports_Ground" title="Albury Sports Ground">Albury Sports Ground</a> and Victorian country towns <a href="/wiki/Yallourn" title="Yallourn">Yallourn</a> and <a href="/wiki/Euroa" title="Euroa">Euroa</a>.
</p><p>Footscray became the first of the 1925 expansion teams to win the premiership in 1954.
</p><p>Melbourne became a powerhouse during the 1950s and early 1960s under coach <a href="/wiki/Norm_Smith" title="Norm Smith">Norm Smith</a> and star player <a href="/wiki/Ron_Barassi" title="Ron Barassi">Ron Barassi</a>. The club contested seven consecutive grand finals from 1954 to 1960, winning five premierships, including three in a row from 1955 to 1957. The became the only club to win the minor premiership 6 times in a row from 1955 to 1960.
</p><p>Television coverage for the VFL commenced in 1957 with direct telecasts of the final quarter permitted. At first, several channels competed through broadcasting different games. When the VFL found that television coverage had reduced crowds, it decided that no television coverage was to be allowed for 1960. In 1961 television replays in Melbourne were introduced although direct telecasts were rarely permitted, compared with the rest of Australia where live telecasts happened every Saturday afternoon.
</p><p>In 1959, the VFL planned the first purpose-built mega-stadium, <a href="/wiki/Waverley_Park" title="Waverley Park">VFL Park (later known as Waverley Park)</a>, to give it some independence from the <a href="/wiki/Melbourne_Cricket_Club" title="Melbourne Cricket Club">Melbourne Cricket Club</a>, which managed the <a href="/wiki/Melbourne_Cricket_Ground" title="Melbourne Cricket Ground">Melbourne Cricket Ground</a>. VFL Park was planned to hold 155,000 spectators, which would have made it one of the largest stadiums in the world – although it would ultimately be built with a capacity of 78,000. Land for the stadium was purchased at Mulgrave, then farmland but predicted to be near the demographic centre of Melbourne's population.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2024)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>The VFL premiership trophy was first awarded in addition to a pennant flag in 1959; essentially the same trophy design has been in use since.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2024)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p>
<figure typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:VFL_Logo_1972-1975.png" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/1/17/VFL_Logo_1972-1975.png/220px-VFL_Logo_1972-1975.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/1/17/VFL_Logo_1972-1975.png/330px-VFL_Logo_1972-1975.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/1/17/VFL_Logo_1972-1975.png/440px-VFL_Logo_1972-1975.png 2x" data-file-width="768" data-file-height="512" /></a><figcaption>VFL Logo used from 1972 to 1975</figcaption></figure>
<p>In the 1960s, television coverage began to have a huge impact on the VFL. Spectators hurried home from games to watch replays and many former players took up positions as commentators on pre-game preview programs and post-game review programs. There were also several attempts at variety programs featuring VFL players, who generally succeeded in demonstrating that their skills were limited to the football ground.
</p><p>The VFL played the first of a series of <a href="/wiki/Australian_rules_football_exhibition_matches" title="Australian rules football exhibition matches">exhibition matches</a> in 1962 in an effort to lift the international profile of the league. In 1967, district football was expanded throughout all of Victoria, clubs now allocated a country zone in addition to their metropolitan districts.<sup id="cite_ref-history_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-history-10"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>10<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>The 1970 season saw the opening of VFL Park, with the inaugural match being played between Geelong and Fitzroy, on 18 April 1970. Construction work was carried out at the stadium as the 1970s progressed, culminating in the building of the now heritage listed Sir Kenneth Luke Stand. <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_II" title="Elizabeth II">Queen Elizabeth II</a>, was a guest at the game and formally opened the stadium to the public. The <a href="/wiki/1970_VFL_Grand_Final" class="mw-redirect" title="1970 VFL Grand Final">1970 grand final</a> between traditional rivals Carlton and Collingwood, arguably the league's most famous game, saw Carlton recover from a 44-point deficit at half-time to win the game by 10 points, featured a famous <a href="/wiki/Spectacular_mark" title="Spectacular mark">spectacular mark</a> by <a href="/wiki/Alex_Jesaulenko" title="Alex Jesaulenko">Alex Jesaulenko</a> and was witnessed by a record crowd of 121,696.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2024)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="1976–1981:_VFL_leaves_Australian_National_Football_Council"><span id="1976.E2.80.931981:_VFL_leaves_Australian_National_Football_Council"></span>1976–1981: VFL leaves Australian National Football Council</h4><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Australian_Football_League&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: 1976–1981: VFL leaves Australian National Football Council"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Championship_of_Australia" title="Championship of Australia">Championship of Australia</a>, <a href="/wiki/1976_NFL_Championship_Series_(Australia)" title="1976 NFL Championship Series (Australia)">1976 NFL Championship Series (Australia)</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Australian_Football_Championships_Night_Series" class="mw-redirect" title="Australian Football Championships Night Series">Australian Football Championships Night Series</a></div>
<p>In 1976, the <a href="/wiki/Australian_National_Football_Council" title="Australian National Football Council">National Football League</a>, which was the peak national administrative body of Australian rules football at the time, established the <a href="/wiki/NFL_Night_Series" title="NFL Night Series">NFL Night Series</a> to succeed the <a href="/wiki/Championship_of_Australia" title="Championship of Australia">Championship of Australia</a>. The Night Series was played concurrently with the premiership season and was contested among twelve clubs from the VFL, <a href="/wiki/South_Australian_National_Football_League" title="South Australian National Football League">SANFL</a> and <a href="/wiki/West_Australian_Football_League" title="West Australian Football League">WAFL</a>, invited based on their finishing positions from the previous year. The event was mostly played on Tuesday nights, with night games at <a href="/wiki/Norwood_Oval" title="Norwood Oval">Norwood Oval</a> in Adelaide and all games were televised live in colour on <a href="/wiki/Nine_Network" title="Nine Network">Channel 9</a>, which opened up unprecedented revenue streams from television rights and sponsorship opportunities for the sport.<sup id="cite_ref-nightseries_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nightseries-11"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>11<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The NFL began plans to expand its Night Series to incorporate more teams from the VFL, SANFL and WAFL, as well as state representative teams from other states.
</p><p>In November 1976, the VFL announced that it was withdrawing from the NFL's competition, having arranged more substantial television and sponsorship deals for its own, rival night competition for 1977 to be based in Melbourne and feature only the VFL clubs. Light towers were erected at VFL Park specifically for the event.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>12<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>13<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The VFL established a <a href="/wiki/Proprietary_limited_company" class="mw-redirect" title="Proprietary limited company">proprietary limited company</a> called Australian Football Championships Pty Ltd in 1978 to run its night competition and offered shareholdings to the other state leagues in an attempt to lure other states into the competition.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>14<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>For the three years from 1977 until 1979, the NFL and VFL night competitions were run separately as rival night competitions. In 1978, the <a href="/wiki/Tasmania_Australian_rules_football_team" class="mw-redirect" title="Tasmania Australian rules football team">Tasmanian representative team</a> competed in both the NFL and VFL night competitions but all SANFL and WAFL clubs and the minor states teams remained in the NFL Night Series. In 1979, the WAFL clubs and the New South Wales and A.C.T. representative teams defected from the NFL Night Series and joined the VFL's night competition, leaving the NFL Night Series mostly composed of SANFL teams. The NFL Night Series was not revived in 1980 and the SANFL clubs joined the VFL's night competition.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>15<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Although the NFL itself continued to exist as an administrative body into the early 1990s, the power gained by the VFL as a result of its take-over of night competition was one of the first significant steps in the VFL's spread interstate and ultimately its take-over and control of <a href="/wiki/Australian_rules_football" title="Australian rules football">Australian football</a> across Australia.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>16<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<figure typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:VFL_Logo_1976-1989.png" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/d/da/VFL_Logo_1976-1989.png/250px-VFL_Logo_1976-1989.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/d/da/VFL_Logo_1976-1989.png/330px-VFL_Logo_1976-1989.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/d/da/VFL_Logo_1976-1989.png/500px-VFL_Logo_1976-1989.png 2x" data-file-width="768" data-file-height="512" /></a><figcaption>VFL Logo used from 1973 to 1989<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>17<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></figcaption></figure>
<p>In 1980 and 1981, the first years after the NFL Night Series ended, the VFL night competition was at its largest, with all VFL, WAFL and SANFL clubs plus the four minor states' teams (selected under residential qualification rather than <a href="/wiki/State_of_origin" class="mw-redirect" title="State of origin">state of origin</a> qualification) competing for a total of 34 teams. In 1982, the size of the competition was reduced and, thereafter, only the top two or three teams from the SANFL and WAFL, as well as the winner of the minor states' annual carnival were invited.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2024)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>In 1987, the night competition reverted to include only the VFL teams. The competition was pushed earlier into the year, with the final played on 28 April.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>18<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The following season, the competition did not overlap with the day premiership season at all and became entirely a <a href="/wiki/Australian_Football_League_pre-season_competition" class="mw-redirect" title="Australian Football League pre-season competition">pre-season competition</a>. The night competition is generally considered<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Words_to_watch#Unsupported_attributions" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Words to watch"><span title="The material near this tag may use weasel words or too-vague attribution. (January 2023)">by whom?</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> to be of equivalent importance as the pre-season competition and the <a href="/wiki/VFL_Night_Series" class="mw-redirect" title="VFL Night Series">VFL Night Series</a> (1956–1971) and records relating to the three competitions are often combined.
</p><p>With the number of players recruited from country leagues increasing, the wealthier VFL clubs were gaining an advantage that metropolitan <a href="/wiki/Zoning_(Australian_rules_football)" title="Zoning (Australian rules football)">zoning</a> and the Coulter law (salary cap) restricting player payments had prevented in the past. Country zoning was introduced in the late 1960s and while it pushed Essendon and Geelong from the top of the ladder, it created severe inequality during the 1970s and 1980s. Between 1972 and 1987, only six of the league's twelve clubs – Carlton, Collingwood, Essendon, Hawthorn, North Melbourne and Richmond – played in grand finals.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="1982–1989:_Professionalism,_club_bankruptcy_and_expansion"><span id="1982.E2.80.931989:_Professionalism.2C_club_bankruptcy_and_expansion"></span>1982–1989: Professionalism, club bankruptcy and expansion</h4><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Australian_Football_League&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: 1982–1989: Professionalism, club bankruptcy and expansion"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Proposed_VFL/AFL_clubs" class="mw-redirect" title="Proposed VFL/AFL clubs">Proposed VFL/AFL clubs</a></div>

</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>The 1980s was a period of significant structural change in Australian football around the country. The VFL was dominant among the Australian football leagues around the country in terms of overall attendance, interest and money and began to look towards expanding its influence directly into other states. The VFL and its top clubs were asserting their financial power to recruit top players from interstate. The resulting rising cost pressures drove the VFL's weaker clubs into dire financial situations. The South Melbourne Swans became the first VFL team to relocate interstate. The South Melbourne Football Club was deeply indebted, including to the VFL which took over the club's Swans team and moved the team's home games to Sydney in 1982 and renamed the team the <a href="/wiki/Sydney_Swans" title="Sydney Swans">Sydney Swans</a> the following year. Under the private ownership of <a href="/wiki/Dr_Geoffrey_Edelsten" class="mw-redirect" title="Dr Geoffrey Edelsten">Dr Geoffrey Edelsten</a> during the mid-1980s, the Sydney Swans became successful on-field. Moving the Swans team to Sydney effectively shifted the debts of a Melbourne club onto Australian football in Sydney and re-directed support and finance to the Swans team to the detriment of existing Australian Football clubs and league competitions in Sydney. However, the Swans team attracted new prominence and supporters for the sport. Despite becoming successful on the field, a succession of owners and transfer to its supporter "members", the Sydney Swans remain indebted to the AFL<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>22<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and subject to its veto control and reversion rights<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>23<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> in what became a model for the AFL control of teams.
</p><p>Throughout the 1980s, approaches were made by SANFL and WAFL clubs to enter the VFL. Of particular note were approaches by the <a href="/wiki/East_Perth_Royals" class="mw-redirect" title="East Perth Royals">East Perth Royals</a> in 1980,<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>24<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/Norwood_Redlegs" class="mw-redirect" title="Norwood Redlegs">Norwood Redlegs</a> in 1986<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>25<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and 1988,<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>26<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and an <a href="/wiki/East_Fremantle_Football_Club" title="East Fremantle Football Club">East</a>–<a href="/wiki/South_Fremantle_Football_Club" title="South Fremantle Football Club">South Fremantle</a> merger proposal in 1987.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>27<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> None of these attempts were successful despite Norwood trying again in 1990 and 1994.
</p><p>In 1986, the <a href="/wiki/West_Australian_Football_League" title="West Australian Football League">West Australian Football League</a> and <a href="/wiki/AFL_Queensland" title="AFL Queensland">Queensland Australian Football League</a> were awarded licences to field expansion teams in the VFL, leading to the establishment of the clubs in Brisbane and Perth (<a href="/wiki/Brisbane_Bears" title="Brisbane Bears">Brisbane Bears</a> and <a href="/wiki/West_Coast_Eagles" title="West Coast Eagles">West Coast Eagles</a>), who both joined the league in 1987. These <a href="/wiki/Expansion_team" title="Expansion team">expansion team</a> licences were awarded on payment of multimillion-dollar fees which were not required of the existing VFL clubs. In 1989 financial troubles nearly forced <a href="/wiki/Footscray_Football_Club" class="mw-redirect" title="Footscray Football Club">Footscray</a> and <a href="/wiki/Fitzroy_Football_Club" title="Fitzroy Football Club">Fitzroy</a> to merge but fees paid by the Brisbane Bears and West Coast Eagles, propped up the struggling VFL sides.
</p><p>The 1980s first saw new regular timeslots for VFL matches. VFL matches had previously been played on Saturday afternoons but Sydney began playing its home matches on Sunday afternoons and North Melbourne pioneered playing matches on Friday night. These have since become regular timeslots for all teams.
</p><p>The first <a href="/wiki/AFL_Draft" class="mw-redirect" title="AFL Draft">national draft</a> was introduced in 1986 and a <a href="/wiki/Salary_cap" title="Salary cap">salary cap</a> was introduced in 1987. District football within Victoria was discontinued around the same time.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="AFL_era_(1990–present)"><span id="AFL_era_.281990.E2.80.93present.29"></span>AFL era (1990–present)</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Australian_Football_League&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: AFL era (1990–present)"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<figure typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:AFL_Logo_1990-1999.png" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/8/85/AFL_Logo_1990-1999.png/250px-AFL_Logo_1990-1999.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/8/85/AFL_Logo_1990-1999.png/330px-AFL_Logo_1990-1999.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/8/85/AFL_Logo_1990-1999.png/500px-AFL_Logo_1990-1999.png 2x" data-file-width="768" data-file-height="512" /></a><figcaption>AFL Logo used from 1990 to 1999</figcaption></figure>
<p>The league was renamed the Australian Football League in 1990 to reflect its national composition.<sup id="cite_ref-Football_Ltd_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Football_Ltd-28"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>28<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="1990–2010:_A_professional_national_competition"><span id="1990.E2.80.932010:_A_professional_national_competition"></span>1990–2010: A professional national competition</h4><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Australian_Football_League&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: 1990–2010: A professional national competition"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>In 1990 the <a href="/wiki/AFL_Players_Association" title="AFL Players Association">AFLPA</a>, the players union, signed its first Collective Bargaining Agreement (CBA) with the league which outlined wages and conditions in what was becoming a sole source of income for players who had previously had part-time or full-time jobs outside of football.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>29<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Functionally, the AFL gave up control over its Victorian-based <a href="/wiki/Australian_Football_League_reserves_affiliations" title="Australian Football League reserves affiliations">minor grades</a> at the end of 1991 – clubs continued to field reserves teams in a <a href="/wiki/AFL_reserves" title="AFL reserves">competition</a> run by the new <a href="/wiki/Victorian_State_Football_League" title="Victorian State Football League">Victorian State Football League</a> and the under-19s competition and zone-based recruiting were abolished and replaced with an <a href="/wiki/NAB_League" class="mw-redirect" title="NAB League">independent system</a>.
</p><p>Midway through 1990, the SANFL's most successful club, <a href="/wiki/Port_Adelaide_Football_Club" title="Port Adelaide Football Club">Port Adelaide</a>, made a bid for an AFL licence. In response, the SANFL gained an injunction via <a href="/wiki/Glenelg_Football_Club" title="Glenelg Football Club">Glenelg</a> and <a href="/wiki/Norwood_Football_Club" title="Norwood Football Club">Norwood</a> against <a href="/wiki/Port_Adelaide_Football_Club" title="Port Adelaide Football Club">Port Adelaide</a>, allowing it time to establish a composite South Australian team called the <a href="/wiki/Adelaide_Crows" class="mw-redirect" title="Adelaide Crows">Adelaide Crows</a>, which was awarded the licence and joined the league in 1991 as the fourth non-Victorian club. The same year saw the West Coast Eagles become the first non-Victorian club to reach the grand final, which was won by Hawthorn. The Eagles would then win the premiership in 1992 and 1994. In 1994, <a href="/wiki/Fremantle_Football_Club" title="Fremantle Football Club">Fremantle</a> obtained an AFL licence and joined the AFL in 1995, becoming the fifth non-Victorian club, and the second from Western Australia.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>30<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Victorian_Football_Association" class="mw-redirect" title="Victorian Football Association">VFA</a> took over the <a href="/wiki/Victorian_Football_League" title="Victorian Football League">Victorian Football League</a> name in 1996.<sup id="cite_ref-Football_Ltd_28-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Football_Ltd-28"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>28<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In 1996 several Victorian clubs were in severe financial difficulties, most notably Fitzroy and Hawthorn. Hawthorn proposed to merge with Melbourne to form the <a href="/wiki/Melbourne_Hawks" title="Melbourne Hawks">Melbourne Hawks</a> but the merger ultimately fell through and both teams continued as separate entities. Fitzroy, however, was too weak to continue by itself. The club nearly merged with North Melbourne to form the <a href="/wiki/Fitzroy-North_Melbourne_Kangaroos_Football_Club" class="mw-redirect" title="Fitzroy-North Melbourne Kangaroos Football Club">Fitzroy-North Melbourne Kangaroos</a> but the other clubs voted against it. In 1994 Port Adelaide was awarded an AFL licence but could not enter until a Victorian team had folded or merged. At the end of 1996 Fitzroy played its last match and merged with Brisbane to form the Brisbane Lions.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>31<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> This allowed Port Adelaide to enter the AFL for the 1997 season as the sixth and only pre-existing non Victorian club.
</p><p>Through the 1990s there was a significant trend of Melbourne-based teams abandoning the use of their small (20,000–30,000 capacity) suburban venues for home matches in favour of the <a href="/wiki/Melbourne_Cricket_Ground" title="Melbourne Cricket Ground">MCG</a> and <a href="/wiki/Waverley_Park" title="Waverley Park">VFL Park</a>, which have and had larger seating capacities. The 1990s saw the last matches played at <a href="/wiki/Windy_Hill,_Essendon" title="Windy Hill, Essendon">Windy Hill</a> (Essendon), <a href="/wiki/Moorabbin_Oval" title="Moorabbin Oval">Moorabbin Oval</a> (St Kilda), <a href="/wiki/Western_Oval" class="mw-redirect" title="Western Oval">Western Oval</a> (Footscray) and <a href="/wiki/Victoria_Park,_Melbourne" title="Victoria Park, Melbourne">Victoria Park</a> (Collingwood) and saw <a href="/wiki/Visy_Park" class="mw-redirect" title="Visy Park">Princes Park</a> abandoned by its long-term co-tenant, Hawthorn. The transition to the use of only two venues in Melbourne was ultimately completed in 2005 when Carlton abandoned the use of Princes Park. In 1999, the league sold <a href="/wiki/Waverley_Park" title="Waverley Park">VFL Park</a> and used the funds in a joint venture to begin construction of a brand-new stadium situated at Melbourne's <a href="/wiki/Melbourne_Docklands" class="mw-redirect" title="Melbourne Docklands">Docklands</a>. Representative state football came to an end, with the last <a href="/wiki/State_of_Origin_(Australian_rules_football)" class="mw-redirect" title="State of Origin (Australian rules football)">State of Origin</a> match held in 1999.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="2011–present:_18-team_era"><span id="2011.E2.80.93present:_18-team_era"></span>2011–present: 18-team era</h4><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Australian_Football_League&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: 2011–present: 18-team era"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>In the late 2000s, the AFL looked to establish a permanent presence in <a href="/wiki/Gold_Coast,_Queensland" title="Gold Coast, Queensland">Gold Coast</a>, <a href="/wiki/Queensland" title="Queensland">Queensland</a>, which was fast-developing as a major population centre. North Melbourne, which was in financial difficulty and had played a few home games on the Gold Coast in previous years, was offered significant subsidies to relocate to the Gold Coast but declined.<br />The AFL then began work to establish a club on the Gold Coast as a new expansion team.
</p><p>Early in 2008, a meeting held by the AFL discussed having two new teams enter the AFL competition.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>32<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In March 2008, the AFL won the support of the league's 16 club presidents to establish sides on the <a href="/wiki/Gold_Coast,_Queensland" title="Gold Coast, Queensland">Gold Coast</a> and in <a href="/wiki/Western_Sydney" class="mw-redirect" title="Western Sydney">Western Sydney</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Gold_Coast_Suns" title="Gold Coast Suns">Gold Coast Suns</a> were established and joined the AFL in 2011 as the 17th team.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>33<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Greater_Western_Sydney_Giants" title="Greater Western Sydney Giants">Greater Western Sydney Giants</a>, representing both Western Sydney and Canberra, were then established and entered the league as the 18th team in 2012.
</p><p>On 25 April 2013 the <a href="/wiki/Westpac_Stadium" class="mw-redirect" title="Westpac Stadium">Westpac Stadium</a> in <a href="/wiki/Wellington" title="Wellington">Wellington</a>, New Zealand hosted the first ever Australian Football League game played for premiership points outside Australia. The night game between <a href="/wiki/St_Kilda_Football_Club" title="St Kilda Football Club">St Kilda</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sydney_Swans" title="Sydney Swans">Sydney</a> was played in front of a crowd of 22,183 on <a href="/wiki/Anzac_Day" title="Anzac Day">Anzac Day</a> to honour the <a href="/wiki/Anzac" class="mw-redirect" title="Anzac">Anzac</a> bond between the two countries.<sup id="cite_ref-stk-rp_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-stk-rp-34"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>34<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-age-aflkiwi_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-age-aflkiwi-35"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>35<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>A <a href="/wiki/AFL_Women%27s" title="AFL Women&#39;s">national women's league</a> comprising a subset of AFL clubs began in 2017. Thirteen AFL clubs placed bids to participate in the women's competition. Eight clubs – <a href="/wiki/Adelaide_Football_Club" title="Adelaide Football Club">Adelaide</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brisbane_Lions" title="Brisbane Lions">Brisbane Lions</a>, <a href="/wiki/Carlton_Football_Club" title="Carlton Football Club">Carlton</a>, <a href="/wiki/Collingwood_Football_Club" title="Collingwood Football Club">Collingwood</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fremantle_Football_Club" title="Fremantle Football Club">Fremantle</a>, <a href="/wiki/Greater_Western_Sydney_Giants" title="Greater Western Sydney Giants">Greater Western Sydney</a>, <a href="/wiki/Melbourne_Football_Club" title="Melbourne Football Club">Melbourne</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Western_Bulldogs" title="Western Bulldogs">Western Bulldogs</a> – were granted licences to participate in the inaugural season.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>36<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Six clubs joined the league in the coming years; <a href="/wiki/Geelong_Football_Club" title="Geelong Football Club">Geelong</a> and <a href="/wiki/North_Melbourne_Football_Club" title="North Melbourne Football Club">North Melbourne</a> entered the competition in 2019, while <a href="/wiki/Gold_Coast_Suns" title="Gold Coast Suns">Gold Coast</a>, <a href="/wiki/Richmond_Football_Club" title="Richmond Football Club">Richmond</a>, <a href="/wiki/St_Kilda_Football_Club" title="St Kilda Football Club">St Kilda</a> and <a href="/wiki/West_Coast_Eagles" title="West Coast Eagles">West Coast</a> made their debut in 2020.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>37<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The remaining four clubs—<a href="/wiki/Essendon_Football_Club" title="Essendon Football Club">Essendon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hawthorn_Football_Club" title="Hawthorn Football Club">Hawthorn</a>, <a href="/wiki/Port_Adelaide_Football_Club" title="Port Adelaide Football Club">Port Adelaide</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sydney_Swans" title="Sydney Swans">Sydney</a>— entered AFL Women's in the <a href="/wiki/AFL_Women%27s_season_seven" class="mw-redirect" title="AFL Women&#39;s season seven">seventh season</a> in 2022.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>38<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>On 14 May 2017, <a href="/wiki/Port_Adelaide_Football_Club" title="Port Adelaide Football Club">Port Adelaide</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Gold_Coast_Suns" title="Gold Coast Suns">Gold Coast</a> played the first-ever AFL match for premiership points in <a href="/wiki/Shanghai" title="Shanghai">Shanghai</a>, China, attracting a crowd of 10,114 at <a href="/wiki/Jiangwan_Stadium" title="Jiangwan Stadium">Jiangwan Stadium</a>. Port Adelaide won the game by 72 points.
</p><p>In 2020, the AFL season was <a href="/wiki/Impact_of_the_COVID-19_pandemic_on_sports" title="Impact of the COVID-19 pandemic on sports">severely disrupted</a> by the <a href="/wiki/COVID-19_pandemic" title="COVID-19 pandemic">COVID-19 pandemic</a>. The first round of matches was played <a href="/wiki/Behind_closed_doors_(sports)" class="mw-redirect" title="Behind closed doors (sports)">in front of no crowds</a> due to the pandemic, before the season was suspended on 22 March due to health concerns and strict government regulations on non-essential travel. After nearly two months of planning with the assistance of state governments and health officials, the season resumed on 11 June, with the length of the season reduced from 22 matches per team to 17 matches. The grand final was played in October at <a href="/wiki/The_Gabba" title="The Gabba">The Gabba</a> in <a href="/wiki/Brisbane" title="Brisbane">Brisbane</a>, the first time it was held outside of Victoria since the creation of the league due to the spiking cases in that state. The pandemic caused the league to lose out on up to $400 million in anticipated revenue and also precipitated a 20% cut in industry jobs.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>39<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/2021_AFL_Grand_Final" title="2021 AFL Grand Final">2021 grand final</a> was played in September at <a href="/wiki/Perth_Stadium" title="Perth Stadium">Perth Stadium</a> in <a href="/wiki/Perth" title="Perth">Perth</a> because an ongoing <a href="/wiki/COVID-19_lockdowns" title="COVID-19 lockdowns">COVID-19 lockdown</a> prevented the match from being played with spectators at the <a href="/wiki/Melbourne_Cricket_Ground" title="Melbourne Cricket Ground">Melbourne Cricket Ground</a> in <a href="/wiki/Melbourne" title="Melbourne">Melbourne</a>, Victoria. It was the first grand final played in Perth and the second consecutive grand final to be played outside Victoria. The event set a new attendance record for Australian rules football in Western Australia, eclipsing the previous record set in 2018 despite not featuring any WA-based teams and being played during the COVID pandemic.
</p>

<p><br />
The AFL operates on a single table system, with no divisions and conferences, nor <a href="/wiki/Promotion_and_relegation" title="Promotion and relegation">promotion and relegation</a> from other leagues.
</p><p>The league was founded as the Victorian Football League (VFL) in 1897, comprising eight teams only based in the state of <a href="/wiki/Victoria_(Australia)" class="mw-redirect" title="Victoria (Australia)">Victoria</a>. Over the next century, a series of expansions, a relocation, a merger and a club withdrawal saw the league's teams expand to the 18 teams there are today.
</p><p>In 1990, the national nature of the competition resulted in the name change to the Australian Football League (AFL). The current 18 teams are based across five states of Australia; the majority (ten) still remain in Victoria, nine of which are located in the <a href="/wiki/Melbourne" title="Melbourne">Melbourne</a> metropolitan area. The states of <a href="/wiki/New_South_Wales" title="New South Wales">New South Wales</a>, <a href="/wiki/Queensland" title="Queensland">Queensland</a>, <a href="/wiki/South_Australia" title="South Australia">South Australia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Western_Australia" title="Western Australia">Western Australia</a> have two teams each, while <a href="/wiki/Tasmania" title="Tasmania">Tasmania</a> will have a team enter the league in 2028.<sup id="cite_ref-19thteam-ABC_4-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19thteam-ABC-4"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>4<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Australian_Capital_Territory" title="Australian Capital Territory">Australian Capital Territory</a> and <a href="/wiki/Northern_Territory" title="Northern Territory">Northern Territory</a> are the only mainland territories not to have AFL clubs, although the Greater Western Sydney Giants have a contract to play at least three home games in the former until 2032, while at least two games per year is played in the latter.
</p>

<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Former_clubs">Former clubs</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Australian_Football_League&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Former clubs"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>Since the league commenced in 1897 as the VFL, only one club, <a href="/wiki/Melbourne_University_Football_Club" title="Melbourne University Football Club">University</a>, has withdrawn from the competition. It last competed in 1914 and withdrew because, as an amateur club, it was unable to remain competitive in a time when player payments were becoming common;<sup id="cite_ref-The_University_Team_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_University_Team-41"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>41<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-42"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>42<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> the club still competes to this day in the <a href="/wiki/Victorian_Amateur_Football_Association" title="Victorian Amateur Football Association">Victorian Amateur Football Association (VAFA)</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>43<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Two other clubs, <a href="/wiki/Fitzroy_Football_Club" title="Fitzroy Football Club">Fitzroy</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Brisbane_Bears" title="Brisbane Bears">Brisbane Bears</a>, merged in 1996 to form the <a href="/wiki/Brisbane_Lions" title="Brisbane Lions">Brisbane Lions</a>; however, after coming out of financial administration in 1998, Fitzroy resumed its playing operations in 2009 and competes in the <a href="/wiki/Victorian_Amateur_Football_Association" title="Victorian Amateur Football Association">VAFA</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>44<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>

<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Timeline_of_clubs">Timeline of clubs</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Australian_Football_League&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Timeline of clubs"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<div class="timeline-wrapper"><map name="timeline_qj1ykaa5wimvm1gp0h6k8enskifelsr"></map><img usemap="#timeline_qj1ykaa5wimvm1gp0h6k8enskifelsr" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/timeline/qj1ykaa5wimvm1gp0h6k8enskifelsr.png" /></div>
<p><span style="background-color:rgb(178,178,178); color:;">Non-formal/junior competitions †</span><br /><span style="background-color:rgb(168,203,253); color:;">Victorian Football Association (1877) †</span><br /><span style="background-color:rgb(107,139,251); color:;">Victorian Football League (1897, later renamed AFL)</span><br /><span style="background-color:rgb(140,203,55); color:;">Australian Football League (1990, formerly VFL)</span><br /><span style="background-color:rgb(223,102,102); color:;">South Australian National Football League (1877) †</span>
</p><p>† Not all teams shown. These competitions are current.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Venues">Venues</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Australian_Football_League&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Venues"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">For a more comprehensive list, see <a href="/wiki/List_of_Australian_Football_League_grounds" title="List of Australian Football League grounds">List of Australian Football League grounds</a>.</div>
<p>Throughout the history of the VFL/AFL to <a href="/wiki/2023_AFL_season" title="2023 AFL season">2023</a>, there have been 50 grounds used.<sup id="cite_ref-groundslist_45-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-groundslist-45"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>45<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The largest-capacity ground in use is the <a href="/wiki/Melbourne_Cricket_Ground" title="Melbourne Cricket Ground">Melbourne Cricket Ground</a> (MCG), which has a capacity of over 100,000 people and hosts the grand final each year (see <a href="/wiki/AFL_Grand_Final_location_debate" title="AFL Grand Final location debate">AFL Grand Final location debate</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>46<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The MCG is shared by six teams as a home ground, while the other grounds used as home venues by multiple teams are <a href="/wiki/Docklands_Stadium" title="Docklands Stadium">Docklands Stadium</a> in Melbourne (five teams), <a href="/wiki/Adelaide_Oval" title="Adelaide Oval">Adelaide Oval</a> in <a href="/wiki/Adelaide" title="Adelaide">Adelaide</a> (two teams) and <a href="/wiki/Perth_Stadium" title="Perth Stadium">Perth Stadium</a> in <a href="/wiki/Perth" title="Perth">Perth</a> (two teams). The AFL has had exclusive ownership of Docklands Stadium (commercially known as <a href="/wiki/Marvel_Comics" title="Marvel Comics">Marvel</a> Stadium) since late 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-AFLOwners_47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AFLOwners-47"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>47<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Prior to the expansion of the competition, most grounds were located in suburban Melbourne, with <a href="/wiki/Princes_Park_(stadium)" title="Princes Park (stadium)">Princes Park</a>, <a href="/wiki/Victoria_Park,_Melbourne" title="Victoria Park, Melbourne">Victoria Park</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Junction_Oval" title="Junction Oval">Junction Oval</a>, <a href="/wiki/Waverley_Park" title="Waverley Park">Waverley Park</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Lakeside_Stadium" title="Lakeside Stadium">Lake Oval</a> each having hosted over 700 games.<sup id="cite_ref-groundslist_45-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-groundslist-45"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>45<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> However, since the introduction of a national competition, each <a href="/wiki/States_and_territories_of_Australia" title="States and territories of Australia">state and territory</a> of Australia has hosted AFL games.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>48<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> On 25 April 2013 (<a href="/wiki/Anzac_Day" title="Anzac Day">Anzac Day</a>), a match took place between St Kilda and Sydney at <a href="/wiki/Wellington_Regional_Stadium" title="Wellington Regional Stadium">Wellington Regional Stadium</a> in <a href="/wiki/Wellington" title="Wellington">Wellington</a>, New Zealand, being the first AFL match played outside Australia for premiership points.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>49<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Current_venues">Current venues</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Australian_Football_League&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Current venues"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>

<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Players">Players</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Australian_Football_League&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Players"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_current_AFL_team_squads" title="List of current AFL team squads">List of current AFL team squads</a> and <a href="/wiki/Category:VFL/AFL_players" title="Category:VFL/AFL players">Category:VFL/AFL players</a></div>
<figure typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Luke_Hodge_2008.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/Luke_Hodge_2008.jpg/250px-Luke_Hodge_2008.jpg" decoding="async" width="200" height="329" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/Luke_Hodge_2008.jpg/330px-Luke_Hodge_2008.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/a/ae/Luke_Hodge_2008.jpg 2x" data-file-width="398" data-file-height="654" /></a><figcaption><a href="/wiki/Luke_Hodge" title="Luke Hodge">Luke Hodge</a>, the first pick in the <a href="/wiki/2001_AFL_draft" title="2001 AFL draft">2001 AFL draft</a>. Hodge has played the most VFL/AFL games of any <a href="/wiki/Australian_Football_League_draft#Number-one_draft_picks" title="Australian Football League draft">number-one draft pick</a> (346 games played), is the only number-one draft pick to win a <a href="/wiki/Norm_Smith_Medal" title="Norm Smith Medal">Norm Smith Medal</a>, is one of just three number-one draft picks to have won a premiership, and has won the most premierships of any number-one draft pick (4)</figcaption></figure>
<p>AFL players are drawn from a number of sources; however, most players enter the league through the <a href="/wiki/AFL_draft" class="mw-redirect" title="AFL draft">AFL draft</a>, held at the end of each season. A small number of players have converted from other sports, or been recruited internationally. Prior to the nationalisation of the competition, a <a href="/wiki/Zoning_(Australian_rules_football)" title="Zoning (Australian rules football)">zoning system</a> was in place. At the end of the season, the best 22 players and coach from across the competition are selected in the <a href="/wiki/All-Australian_team" title="All-Australian team">All-Australian team</a>.
</p><p>The AFL has tight controls over the player lists of each club. Currently, apart from the recently added expansion clubs who have some additional players, each team can have a senior list of 38 to 40 players plus 4 to 6 <a href="/wiki/Rookie_list" title="Rookie list">rookie players</a>, to a total of 44 players<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>50<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> (following a reduction by two of the number of rookies in 2012) and up to three development rookies (international, alternative talent or New South Wales scholarship players).<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>51<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Changes to playing lists are permitted only in the off-season: clubs can trade players during a <a href="/wiki/AFL_trade_week" title="AFL trade week">trade period</a> which follows each season and recruit new players through the three <a href="/wiki/AFL_draft" class="mw-redirect" title="AFL draft">AFL drafts</a>, the national draft, the <a href="/wiki/AFL_pre-season_draft" title="AFL pre-season draft">pre-season draft</a> and the rookie draft, which take place after the trade period. A mid-year draft was conducted between 1990 and 1993.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>52<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The national draft is the primary method of recruiting new players and has been used since 1986. The draft order is based on reverse-finishing position from the previous year but selections can be traded. <a href="/wiki/Free_agency_(sports)" class="mw-redirect" title="Free agency (sports)">Free agency</a> player movements have only been permitted since the 2012/13 offseason,<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>53<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> previously having been rejected by the AFL.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>54<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Salary_cap">Salary cap</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Australian_Football_League&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Salary cap"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/AFL_salary_cap" title="AFL salary cap">AFL salary cap</a></div>
<p>A <a href="/wiki/Salary_cap" title="Salary cap">salary cap</a> (known as the Total Player Payments or TPP) is also in place as part of the league's equalisation policy; this was $9,130,000 for the 2013 season with a salary floor of $8,673,500 except for the <a href="/wiki/Gold_Coast_Suns" title="Gold Coast Suns">Gold Coast</a>, whose salary cap was $9,630,000 with a salary floor of $9,171,500 and <a href="/wiki/Greater_Western_Sydney_Giants" title="Greater Western Sydney Giants">Greater Western Sydney</a>, whose salary cap was $9,987,000 with a floor of $9,530,500. As part of the AFL's enhanced equalisation policies, in 2014 the league announced an increase of the TPP for the <b>2015</b> and <b>2016</b> seasons. TPP increased an additional $150,000 per club in 2015 above previously contracted amounts, increasing from $9.92m to $10.07m in 2015 and $10.22m to $10.37m in 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>55<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>The salary cap was set at $1.25 million for 1987–1989 as per VFL agreement, with the salary floor set at 90% of the cap or $1.125 million; the salary floor was increased to 92.5% of the cap in 2001 and 95% of the cap for 2013 due to increased revenues. Both the salary cap and salary floor has increased substantially since the competition was rebranded as the AFL in 1990.
</p><p>Salaries of draft selections are fixed for two years. Salaries for senior players are not normally released to the public, though the average AFL player salary at the conclusion of the 2012 season was $251,559<sup id="cite_ref-afl.com.au_56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-afl.com.au-56"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>56<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and the top few players can expect to earn up to and above $1,000,000 a year.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>57<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Upon successfully trading to the <a href="/wiki/Sydney_Swans" title="Sydney Swans">Sydney Swans</a> in 2013, marquee player <a href="/wiki/Lance_Franklin" title="Lance Franklin">Lance Franklin</a> signed a 9-year contract with the club, reportedly worth over $10&#160;million and resulting in subsequent payments of $1.8&#160;million annually in consecutive seasons.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>58<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The Total Player Earnings (TPE) – or total amount of revenue spent on reimbursement of AFL listed players – at the conclusion of the 2012 season was $173.7&#160;million, up by 13 per cent from $153.7&#160;million in 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-afl.com.au_56-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-afl.com.au-56"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>56<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In June 2017, the AFL and <a href="/wiki/AFL_Players_Association" title="AFL Players Association">AFL Players Association</a> agreed to a new <a href="/wiki/Collective_Bargaining_Agreement" class="mw-redirect" title="Collective Bargaining Agreement">CBA</a> deal which resulted in a 20% increase in players' salaries. The six-year deal, which began in 2017 and ends in 2022 means that the average player wage rises from $309,000 to $371,000 and the player salary cap from $10.37m to $12.45m. In 2022, the final year of the agreement, the average player wage will be $389,000 with a salary cap of $13.54m.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>59<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>The breaches of the salary cap and salary floor regulations outlined by the AFL are: exceeding the TPP; falling below the salary floor; not informing the AFL of payments; late or incorrect lodgement or loss of documents; or engaging in draft tampering. Penalties include fines of up to triple the amount involved ($10,000 for each document late or incorrect lodged or lost), forfeiture of draft picks and/or deduction of premiership points. The most significant breach of the salary cap was that of the <a href="/wiki/Carlton_Football_Club_salary_cap_breach" title="Carlton Football Club salary cap breach">Carlton Football Club in the early 2000s</a>.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Demographics">Demographics</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Australian_Football_League&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Demographics"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/List_of_VFL/AFL_players_born_outside_Australia" title="List of VFL/AFL players born outside Australia">List of VFL/AFL players born outside Australia</a>, <a href="/wiki/VFL/AFL_players_with_international_backgrounds" class="mw-redirect" title="VFL/AFL players with international backgrounds">VFL/AFL players with international backgrounds</a>, and <a href="/wiki/List_of_Indigenous_Australian_VFL/AFL_and_AFL_Women%27s_players" title="List of Indigenous Australian VFL/AFL and AFL Women&#39;s players">List of Indigenous Australian VFL/AFL and AFL Women's players</a></div>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1251242444">.mw-parser-output .ambox{border:1px solid #a2a9b1;border-left:10px solid #36c;background-color:#fbfbfb;box-sizing:border-box}.mw-parser-output .ambox-move{border-left:10px solid #9932cc}.mw-parser-output .ambox-protection{border-left:10px solid #a2a9b1}.mw-parser-output .ambox .mbox-text{border:none;padding:0.25em .ambox{margin:0 10%}}@media print{body.ns-0 .mw-parser-output .ambox{display:none!important}}</style><table class="box-Update plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Update" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Ambox_current_red_Asia_Australia.svg/60px-Ambox_current_red_Asia_Australia.svg.png" decoding="async" width="42" height="34"
