article to reflect recent events or newly available information.</span>  <span class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">August 2022</span>)</i></span></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Lance_Franklin_2017.1.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Lance_Franklin_2017.1.jpg/250px-Lance_Franklin_2017.1.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="255" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Lance_Franklin_2017.1.jpg/330px-Lance_Franklin_2017.1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Lance_Franklin_2017.1.jpg/500px-Lance_Franklin_2017.1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="665" data-file-height="999" /></a><figcaption>Indigenous player <a href="/wiki/Lance_Franklin" title="Lance Franklin">Lance Franklin</a>. Although comprising only 2.7% of the broader Australian population, Indigenous Australians make up 9% of AFL players.</figcaption></figure>
<p>There were 801 players on AFL club senior, veteran, rookie and international lists in 2011, including players from every <a href="/wiki/States_of_Australia" class="mw-redirect" title="States of Australia">state and mainland territory</a> of Australia.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>60<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> As of 2014, there were 68 <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_Australian" class="mw-redirect" title="Indigenous Australian">Indigenous Australian</a> players on AFL club lists, comprising approximately 9% of the overall playing population.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>61<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>There were 12 players recruited from outside Australia on AFL lists in 2011, including 10 from <a href="/wiki/Ireland" title="Ireland">Ireland</a>, all <a href="/wiki/List_of_players_who_have_converted_from_one_football_code_to_another" title="List of players who have converted from one football code to another">converts</a> from <a href="/wiki/Gaelic_football" title="Gaelic football">Gaelic football</a> drafted as part of the <a href="/wiki/Irish_Experiment" class="mw-redirect" title="Irish Experiment">Irish Experiment</a> and one each from the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a> and <a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">Canada</a>. There were also another five overseas-born players who emigrated to Australia at an early age on AFL lists.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>62<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>An international rookie list and international scholarship list were introduced in 2006. The international rookie list includes up to two players between the ages of 15 and 23 who are not Australian citizens. These players may remain on this list for up to three years before they must be transferred to the senior or rookie list. For the first year, payments made to international-rookie-listed players fell outside the salary cap. The international scholarship list gives AFL clubs the option of recruiting up to eight players from outside Australia (other than Ireland). Irish players are required to either be placed on clubs' senior or <a href="/wiki/Rookie_list" title="Rookie list">rookie lists</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>63<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> At the beginning of 2011, there were 14 international scholarship players.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>64<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Of the 121 multicultural players, more than half have one parent from <a href="/wiki/Anglophone" class="mw-redirect" title="Anglophone">Anglophone</a> countries, mainly the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a>, Ireland and <a href="/wiki/New_Zealand" title="New Zealand">New Zealand</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>65<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Season_structure">Season structure</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Australian_Football_League&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Season structure"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Pre-season">Pre-season</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Australian_Football_League&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Pre-season"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Australian_Football_League_pre-season_competition" class="mw-redirect" title="Australian Football League pre-season competition">Australian Football League pre-season competition</a></div>
<p>From 1988 until 2013, the AFL ran a pre-season competition that finished prior to the commencement of the premiership season, which served as both warm-up matches for the season and as a stand-alone competition.
</p><p>It was mostly contested as a four-week <a href="/wiki/Knock_out_tournament" class="mw-redirect" title="Knock out tournament">knock out tournament</a> but the format changed after the expansion of the league beyond sixteen clubs in 2011 and has frequently been used to trial rule changes.
</p><p>In 2014, the competition format was abandoned and practice matches are now played under the sponsored name <b>Marsh Community Series</b>. This consists of all 18 clubs playing two matches each, which are played on some weekdays and weekends, throughout February and early March.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Premiership_season">Premiership season</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Australian_Football_League&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Premiership season"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/2025_AFL_season" title="2025 AFL season">2025 AFL season</a></div>
<p>The AFL home-and-away season at present lasts for 24 rounds, starting in mid-March and ending in late August. As of the <a href="/wiki/2025_AFL_season" title="2025 AFL season">2025 AFL season</a>, each team plays 23 matches, consisting of 11 home games, 11 away games, <a href="/wiki/Gather_Round" title="Gather Round">1 neutral game</a>, and one bye. Teams receive four premiership points for a win and two premiership points for a draw. Ladder finishing positions are based on the number of premiership points won. "Percentage", calculated as the ratio of points scored to points conceded throughout the season, is used as a tie-breaker when teams finish with equal premiership points. Further tie-breakers, if required, are the premiership points accumulated in head-to-head matches between the tied teams and then the percentage earned in such matches, with a final tie-breaker being a random drawing of lots.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>66<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="Themed_rounds_and_special_matches">Themed rounds and special matches</h4><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Australian_Football_League&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Themed rounds and special matches"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Anzac_Day_2011_game_3.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Anzac_Day_2011_game_3.jpg/220px-Anzac_Day_2011_game_3.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Anzac_Day_2011_game_3.jpg/330px-Anzac_Day_2011_game_3.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Anzac_Day_2011_game_3.jpg/440px-Anzac_Day_2011_game_3.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1200" /></a><figcaption>The <a href="/wiki/Anzac_Day_clash" class="mw-redirect" title="Anzac Day clash">Anzac Day clash</a>, one of the marquee fixtures in the AFL home and away season</figcaption></figure>
<p>Several teams also play against each other at set times each year, with the most prominent of these being when Collingwood play Essendon in the annual <a href="/wiki/The_Anzac_Day_clash" class="mw-redirect" title="The Anzac Day clash">Anzac Day clash</a> at the MCG.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>67<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Other prominent matches include the <a href="/wiki/King%27s_Birthday_match_(AFL)" title="King&#39;s Birthday match (AFL)">King's Birthday match</a> between Collingwood and Melbourne and the <a href="/wiki/Easter_Monday" title="Easter Monday">Easter Monday</a> clash between Geelong and Hawthorn.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>68<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>69<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>As of November 2023<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Australian_Football_League&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup> the men's league had no plans to introduce a Pride Round in the men's game, although the <a href="/wiki/AFLW" class="mw-redirect" title="AFLW">AFLW</a> had established <a href="/wiki/Pride_Round_(AFLW)" class="mw-redirect" title="Pride Round (AFLW)">their pride round</a> in 2021.<sup id="cite_ref-bourke2023_70-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bourke2023-70"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>70<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>There are <a href="/wiki/List_of_individual_match_awards_in_the_Australian_Football_League" title="List of individual match awards in the Australian Football League">separate trophies</a> for matches between several clubs.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="Sir_Doug_Nicholls_Round">Sir Doug Nicholls Round</h4><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Australian_Football_League&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Sir Doug Nicholls Round"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>Perhaps the most well-known of the themed rounds is the <b>Indigenous Round</b>. In 2007, following the success of the <a href="/wiki/Dreamtime_at_the_%27G" title="Dreamtime at the &#39;G">Dreamtime at the 'G</a> matches in 2005 and 2006, the AFL nominated a specific Indigenous Round (round 9), which has become an annual event in which the Dreamtime at the 'G match takes centre stage on a Saturday night. The success of the annual match, which now usually features crowds in excess of 80,000, led to the two clubs agreeing to cement the match arrangement for an additional decade in May 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>71<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In 2016, the round was named after <a href="/wiki/Sir_Doug_Nicholls" class="mw-redirect" title="Sir Doug Nicholls">Sir Doug Nicholls</a>, the only VFL player to have been <a href="/wiki/Knight_Bachelor" title="Knight Bachelor">knighted</a> and who served as a state <a href="/wiki/Governor_of_South_Australia" title="Governor of South Australia">governor</a> (of <a href="/wiki/South_Australia" title="South Australia">South Australia</a>). The round is now officially named the <b>Sir Doug Nicholls Round</b>.<sup id="cite_ref-Guard_72-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Guard-72"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>72<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>73<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Each year, each player in all 18 clubs wears a specially commissioned artwork by an Indigenous artist on their guernsey,<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>74<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and some clubs rebrand with Indigenous club names in place of their regular names for the duration.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Finals_series">Finals series</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Australian_Football_League&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Finals series"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Australian_Football_League_premiers" class="mw-redirect" title="List of Australian Football League premiers">List of Australian Football League premiers</a></div>
<p>The top eight teams at the end of the AFL Premiership season compete in a four-week <a href="/wiki/AFL_finals_series" title="AFL finals series">finals series</a> throughout September, culminating in a <a href="/wiki/AFL_Grand_Final" title="AFL Grand Final">grand final</a> to determine the premiers. The finals series is played under the <a href="/wiki/AFL_final_eight_system" title="AFL final eight system">AFL final eight system</a>, and the grand final is traditionally played at the <a href="/wiki/Melbourne_Cricket_Ground" title="Melbourne Cricket Ground">Melbourne Cricket Ground</a> on the afternoon of the last Saturday in September.
</p><p>The winning team receives a silver premiership cup, a navy blue premiership flag – a new one of each is manufactured each year – and is recorded on the perpetual E. L. Wilson Shield. The flag has been presented since the league began and is traditionally unfurled at the team's first home game of the following season. The Wilson Shield, named after <a href="/wiki/Edwin_Lionel_Wilson" title="Edwin Lionel Wilson">Edwin Lionel Wilson</a>, was first awarded after the 1929 premiership.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>75<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The premiership cup was first introduced in 1959 and is manufactured annually by Cash's International at their metalworks in <a href="/wiki/Frankston,_Victoria" title="Frankston, Victoria">Frankston, Victoria</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>76<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Additionally, each player in the grand final–winning team receives a premiership medallion.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Awards">Awards</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Australian_Football_League&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Awards"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>The following major individual awards and accolades are presented each season:
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Brownlow_Medal" title="Brownlow Medal">Brownlow Medal</a> – to the <a href="/wiki/Best_and_fairest" title="Best and fairest">fairest and best</a> player in the league, voted by the umpires</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Coleman_Medal" title="Coleman Medal">Coleman Medal</a> – to the player who kicks the most <a href="/wiki/Goal_(Australian_rules_football)" class="mw-redirect" title="Goal (Australian rules football)">goals</a> during the home-and-away season</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/All-Australian_team" title="All-Australian team">All-Australian team</a> – a squad of 22 players deemed the best in their positions, voted by an AFL-appointed committee</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/AFL_Rising_Star" title="AFL Rising Star">Rising Star Award</a> – to the fairest and best young player (under the age of 21 and with fewer than ten games' experience at the beginning of the year), voted by the All-Australian committee</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Norm_Smith_Medal" title="Norm Smith Medal">Norm Smith Medal</a> – the best player on the ground in the grand final, voted by a committee</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Jock_McHale_Medal" class="mw-redirect" title="Jock McHale Medal">Jock McHale Medal</a> – the coach of the premiership-winning team</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Mark_of_the_Year" title="Mark of the Year">Mark of the Year</a> – to the player who takes the best or most <a href="/wiki/Spectacular_mark" title="Spectacular mark">spectacular mark</a> during the season</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Goal_of_the_Year_(Australia)" class="mw-redirect" title="Goal of the Year (Australia)">Goal of the Year</a> – to the player who kicks the best or most spectacular goal during the season</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Leigh_Matthews_Trophy" title="Leigh Matthews Trophy">Leigh Matthews Trophy</a> – to the best player in the league, voted by the players through the <a href="/wiki/AFL_Players%27_Association" class="mw-redirect" title="AFL Players&#39; Association">AFL Players' Association</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Ron_Barassi_Medal" class="mw-redirect" title="Ron Barassi Medal">Ron Barassi Medal</a> - to the winning captain in the Grand Final. Introduced in 2024 in honour of the late <a href="/wiki/Ron_Barassi" title="Ron Barassi">Ron Barassi</a>, who died in September 2023, aged 87. Ron Barassi was an inaugural member and earnt the Legend status within the AFL Hall of Fame when it was founded in 1996. Barassi won 10 premierships, 6 as a player for <a href="/wiki/Melbourne_Demons" class="mw-redirect" title="Melbourne Demons">Melbourne Demons</a> (1955, 1956, 1957, 1959, 1960, and 1964) and 4 as a coach (2 with the <a href="/wiki/Carlton_Blues" class="mw-redirect" title="Carlton Blues">Carlton Blues</a> in 1968 &amp; 1970, and the other 2 with the <a href="/wiki/North_Melbourne_Kangaroos" class="mw-redirect" title="North Melbourne Kangaroos">North Melbourne Kangaroos</a> in 1975 &amp; 1977). AFL Chief Executive <a href="/wiki/Andrew_Dillon" title="Andrew Dillon">Andrew Dillon</a> said, "it was only fitting the Ron Barassi Medal was now etched into our game's history".<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>77<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li></ul>
<p>Other independent <a href="/wiki/Best_and_fairest" title="Best and fairest">best and fairest</a> awards are presented by different football and media organisations.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Team_of_the_Century">Team of the Century</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Australian_Football_League&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Team of the Century"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>To celebrate the 100th season of the VFL/AFL, the "AFL Team of the Century" was named in 1996.
</p>

<p><a href="/wiki/Jack_Elder_(umpire)" title="Jack Elder (umpire)">Jack Elder</a> was declared the <i>Umpire of the Century</i> to coincide with the Team of the Century. Since the naming of this side, most AFL clubs have nominated their own teams of the century. An <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_Team_of_the_Century" title="Indigenous Team of the Century">Indigenous Team of the Century</a> was also selected in 2005, featuring the best Aboriginal players of the previous 100 years from both the VFL/AFL and other state leagues.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Representative_football">Representative football</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Australian_Football_League&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Representative football"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="State_football">State football</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Australian_Football_League&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: State football"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Interstate_matches_in_Australian_rules_football" title="Interstate matches in Australian rules football">Interstate matches in Australian rules football</a></div>
<p>State representation football in the AFL initially ended in 1999. The concept has been revived twice since then in 2008 and 2020 when a Victorian state team took on all stars teams (in 2008 against <i>The Dream Team</i> and in 2020 against the <i>All Stars</i>).<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>78<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>79<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="History_of_the_VFL/AFL's_involvement"><span id="History_of_the_VFL.2FAFL.27s_involvement"></span>History of the VFL/AFL's involvement</h4><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Australian_Football_League&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: History of the VFL/AFL&#39;s involvement"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Ted_Whitten_statue.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Ted_Whitten_statue.jpg/250px-Ted_Whitten_statue.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="255" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Ted_Whitten_statue.jpg/330px-Ted_Whitten_statue.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Ted_Whitten_statue.jpg/500px-Ted_Whitten_statue.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3744" data-file-height="5616" /></a><figcaption>Statue of Footscray legend and leading State of Origin proponent <a href="/wiki/Ted_Whitten" title="Ted Whitten">Ted Whitten</a>, after whom the <a href="/wiki/E._J._Whitten_Legends_Game" title="E. J. Whitten Legends Game">E. J. Whitten Legends Game</a> is named</figcaption></figure>
<p>VFL players first represented the Victoria representative team in 1897 regardless of their state of origin.
</p><p>Being the dominant league drawing many of the country's best players, the <a href="/wiki/Victoria_Australian_rules_football_team" title="Victoria Australian rules football team">Victoria Australian rules football team</a> (nicknamed the "Big V" and composed mostly of VFL players) dominated interstate matches until the introduction of State of Origin selection criteria by the <a href="/wiki/Australian_National_Football_Council" title="Australian National Football Council">Australian Football Council</a> in 1977, after which Victoria's results with the other main Australian football states became more even.
</p><p>The AFL assumed control of interstate football in 1993<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="Please clarify the preceding statement or statements with a good explanation from a reliable source. (January 2023)">how?</span></a></i>&#93;</sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="The text near this tag needs further explanation. (January 2023)">further explanation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2023)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> and coordinated an annual <a href="/wiki/Representative_matches_in_Australian_rules_football" class="mw-redirect" title="Representative matches in Australian rules football">State of Origin</a> series typically held during a mid-season bye round.
</p><p>However, after the 1999 series, the AFL declared the concept of interstate football "on hold", citing club unwillingness to release star players and a lack of public interest. Indeed, the 1999 series, where Victoria defeated South Australia by 54 points, was played in wet conditions in front of a crowd of 26,063, whereas 10 years earlier, the same match-up with a plethora of star players attracted a crowd of 91,960.
</p><p>The AFL shifted its focus of representative football to the International Rules Series, where at the time in the late 1990s, drew a greater television revenue. A once-off representative match, known as the <a href="/wiki/AFL_Hall_of_Fame_Tribute_Match" title="AFL Hall of Fame Tribute Match">AFL Hall of Fame Tribute Match</a>, was played in 2008 to celebrate the 150th anniversary of the sport between a team of players of Victorian origin and a team of players of interstate origin (the "Dream Team"), which was won by Victoria.
</p><p>In 2020, the AFL hosted a <a href="/wiki/State_of_Origin_for_Bushfire_Relief_Match" title="State of Origin for Bushfire Relief Match">special one-off State of Origin match</a>, with the money raised from the event going towards affected bushfire communities. On 28 February, the game took place at Marvel Stadium, with Victoria defeating an All-Stars team and <a href="/wiki/Dustin_Martin" title="Dustin Martin">Dustin Martin</a> being declared best on ground.
</p><p>Since 1996, some past AFL players participated and helped with the promotion of the <a href="/wiki/E._J._Whitten_Legends_Game" title="E. J. Whitten Legends Game">E. J. Whitten Legends Game</a>, although this, too, was put on indefinite hiatus following the 2019 edition.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Global_market">Global market</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Australian_Football_League&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Global market"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>Although no <a href="/wiki/Professional_sports" title="Professional sports">professional</a> leagues or teams exist outside Australia, the AFL has stated that it wishes to showcase Australian rules football to other countries such as the United States of America to create a global following, thus creating more exposure for its sponsors in the increasing North America markets.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>80<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>81<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> On 17 October 2010, AFL clubs <a href="/wiki/Melbourne_Football_Club" title="Melbourne Football Club">Melbourne Demons</a> and <a href="/wiki/Brisbane_Lions" title="Brisbane Lions">Brisbane Lions</a> played an exhibition game in front of 7,000 people at the <a href="/wiki/Jiangwan_Sports_Center" class="mw-redirect" title="Jiangwan Sports Center">Jiangwan Sports Center</a> in Shanghai.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>82<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> This was the first professional AFL game to be played in China. Since then, AFL premiership matches have been played in New Zealand and China, and the competition developed some interest in North America amidst the <a href="/wiki/COVID-19_pandemic" title="COVID-19 pandemic">COVID-19 pandemic</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>83<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="International_Rules_Series">International Rules Series</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Australian_Football_League&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: International Rules Series"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/International_rules_football" title="International rules football">International rules football</a></div>
<p>The AFL has garnered increased interest in Ireland due to the introduction of the <a href="/wiki/International_Rules_Series" title="International Rules Series">International Rules Series</a> played between an AFL-picked <a href="/wiki/Australia_international_rules_football_team" class="mw-redirect" title="Australia international rules football team">Australian Team</a> (sourced entirely from <a href="/wiki/All-Australian_team" title="All-Australian team">All-Australian</a> players since 2004) and <a href="/wiki/Ireland_international_rules_football_team" class="mw-redirect" title="Ireland international rules football team">Ireland international rules football team</a> beginning from 1984. The series is organised under the auspices of the AFL and the <a href="/wiki/Gaelic_Athletic_Association" title="Gaelic Athletic Association">Gaelic Athletic Association</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>84<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The game itself is a <a href="/wiki/Hybrid_sport" class="mw-redirect" title="Hybrid sport">hybrid sport</a>, consisting of rules from both Australian football and Gaelic football. The series provides the only outlet for AFL players to represent their nation.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>85<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> This series encouraged young Irish footballers switching code to join AFL teams because, whilst the <a href="/wiki/Gaelic_Football" class="mw-redirect" title="Gaelic Football">Gaelic Football</a> is strictly amateur, the AFL is fully professional, thus players can make a living out of playing AFL. However, some Irish players fail to make the grade into the very competitive AFL.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>86<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> This also paved the way for extended news coverage and increased broadcasting in the United Kingdom and Ireland.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2012)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>Around the same time that the inaugural International Rules Series commenced, <a href="/wiki/Australian_Football_Hall_of_Fame#Legends" title="Australian Football Hall of Fame">Australian Football Hall of Fame Legend</a> <a href="/wiki/Ron_Barassi" title="Ron Barassi">Ron Barassi</a> launched the <a href="/wiki/Irish_experiment_(Australian_rules_football)" title="Irish experiment (Australian rules football)">Irish experiment</a>, which scouted and recruited dozens of Irishmen (usually Gaelic footballers) with potential for crossing over to playing in the AFL. This resulted in successful recruitmant and training of Australian Hall of Famer <a href="/wiki/Jim_Stynes" title="Jim Stynes">Jim Stynes</a> among other successful players.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Corporate_governance">Corporate governance</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Australian_Football_League&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Corporate governance"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/AFL_Commission" title="AFL Commission">AFL Commission</a></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_VFL/AFL_commissioners_and_club_presidents" title="List of VFL/AFL commissioners and club presidents">List of VFL/AFL commissioners and club presidents</a></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Gillon_McLachlan_03.02.201.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Gillon_McLachlan_03.02.201.jpg/170px-Gillon_McLachlan_03.02.201.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="250" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Gillon_McLachlan_03.02.201.jpg/255px-Gillon_McLachlan_03.02.201.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Gillon_McLachlan_03.02.201.jpg/340px-Gillon_McLachlan_03.02.201.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1838" data-file-height="2708" /></a><figcaption><a href="/wiki/Gillon_McLachlan" title="Gillon McLachlan">Gillon McLachlan</a>, Former CEO of the AFL</figcaption></figure>
<p>The AFL is governed by directors known as the <a href="/wiki/AFL_Commission" title="AFL Commission">AFL Commission</a>. The commission was established in December 1985 and replaced the board of directors elected by and representing the original member clubs in 1993,<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>87<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> after the club parochialism and self-interest which came with the traditional club delegate based administrative structure threatened to undermine the competition.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="The text near this tag needs further explanation. (January 2023)">further explanation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2023)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>The commission chairman is <a href="/wiki/Richard_Goyder" title="Richard Goyder">Richard Goyder</a>, who took over from <a href="/wiki/Mike_Fitzpatrick_(footballer)" title="Mike Fitzpatrick (footballer)">Mike Fitzpatrick</a> on 4 April 2017. The CEO of the AFL is <a href="/wiki/Andrew_Dillon_(sports_administrator)" title="Andrew Dillon (sports administrator)">Andrew Dillon</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>88<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>89<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In addition to administering the national competition, the AFL is heavily involved in promoting and developing the sport in Australia. It provides funds for local leagues and in conjunction with local clubs, administers the <a href="/wiki/Auskick" title="Auskick">Auskick</a> program for young boys and girls.
</p><p>The AFL also plays a leading role in developing the game outside Australia, with projects to develop the game at junior level in other countries (e.g. South Africa) and by supporting affiliated competitions around the world (See <a href="/wiki/Australian_football_around_the_world" class="mw-redirect" title="Australian football around the world">Australian football around the world</a>).
</p><p>The players of the AFL are represented by the <a href="/wiki/AFL_Players_Association" title="AFL Players Association">AFL Players Association</a>, the coaches are represented by the <a href="/wiki/AFL_Coaches_Association" title="AFL Coaches Association">AFL Coaches Association</a>, the umpires are represented by the <a href="/wiki/AFL_Umpires_Association" title="AFL Umpires Association">AFL Umpires Association</a> and the related media employees are represented by the Australian Football Media Association.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Audience">Audience</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Australian_Football_League&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Audience"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>The AFL was the <a href="/wiki/2012_Australian_football_code_crowds" title="2012 Australian football code crowds">best-attended sporting league in Australia in 2012</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>90<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> According to market research, the AFL is the second-most-watched sporting event in Australia, behind <a href="/wiki/Cricket" title="Cricket">cricket</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>91<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Currently, broadcast rights for the AFL are shared between the <a href="/wiki/Seven_Network" title="Seven Network">Seven Network</a> (<a href="/wiki/Free-to-air" title="Free-to-air">free-to-air</a>), <a href="/wiki/Foxtel" title="Foxtel">Foxtel</a> (pay TV) and <a href="/wiki/Kayo_Sports" title="Kayo Sports">Kayo Sports</a> (internet). In 2019, a record 1,057,572 people were members of an AFL club.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>92<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> TV audiences during the <a href="/wiki/2022_AFL_season" title="2022 AFL season">2022 AFL season</a> totalled 125.4 million viewers, with an average of 537,000 people watching each match; the TV audience for the <a href="/wiki/2023_AFL_Grand_Final" title="2023 AFL Grand Final">2023 AFL Grand Final</a> was 4.98 million—plus an additional 756,000 on <a href="/wiki/7plus" title="7plus">7plus</a>, for a total of 5.736 million<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>93<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>94<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>95<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>—and the game was seen by 100,024 stadium spectators, which was exactly the same as the <a href="/wiki/2022_AFL_Grand_Final" title="2022 AFL Grand Final">2022 AFL Grand Final</a>. Excluding the grand final (which is exclusive to Seven Network in Australia), 54% of viewers watched using the paid services of Foxtel or Kayo in 2022, while 46% watched the Seven Network's free-to-air broadcasts.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>96<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>

<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Television">Television</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Australian_Football_League&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Television"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="Australian_television">Australian television</h4><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Australian_Football_League&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Australian television"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Australian_Football_League_television_shows" title="List of Australian Football League television shows">List of Australian Football League television shows</a></div><p>AFL matches are currently broadcast in Australia by the free-to-air <a href="/wiki/Seven_Network" title="Seven Network">Seven Network</a> and subscription television provider <a href="/wiki/Foxtel" title="Foxtel">Foxtel</a>. The current deal was announced in August 2015 and covered the inclusive 2017–2022 seasons.<sup id="cite_ref-CurrentTVrightsOverview_98-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CurrentTVrightsOverview-98"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>98<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In 2020, the deal was extended until 2024 inclusive.
</p><p>The Seven Network broadcasts an average of three-and-a-half games a round; Friday Night, Saturday Night, Sunday Afternoon and any Thursday or Monday Night matches that may occur throughout the year. Channel Seven also airs the AFL Finals Series and the <a href="/wiki/AFL_Grand_Final" title="AFL Grand Final">AFL Grand Final</a>. Foxtel broadcasts every match through their <a href="/wiki/Fox_Footy" title="Fox Footy">Fox Footy</a> channels, including simulcasts from the Seven Network except for the grand final, which is aired exclusively on Channel Seven. Foxtel also has the rights to air rounds on their internet protocol television platform titled <a href="/wiki/Foxtel_Now" title="Foxtel Now">Foxtel Now</a>, as well as via the sports streaming service <a href="/wiki/Kayo_Sports" title="Kayo Sports">Kayo</a>.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="Telecast_history">Telecast history</h4><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Australian_Football_League&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: Telecast history"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>The 1957 VFL season was the first broadcast after the commencement of television in Australia (introduced in 1956 to coincide with the <a href="/wiki/Melbourne_Olympic_Games" class="mw-redirect" title="Melbourne Olympic Games">Melbourne Olympic Games</a>). During the late 1950s and 1960s, all Melbourne stations (<a href="/wiki/ABV2" class="mw-redirect" title="ABV2">ABV2</a>, <a href="/wiki/HSV7" class="mw-redirect" title="HSV7">HSV7</a>, <a href="/wiki/GTV9" class="mw-redirect" title="GTV9">GTV9</a> and, after it commenced in 1965, <a href="/wiki/ATV10" class="mw-redirect" title="ATV10">ATV0/ATV10</a>) broadcast some games. However, in the late 1950s and early 1960s, the VFL was concerned that direct telecasts may affect attendances and stations were only permitted to telecast a delayed replay of the last quarter of games. From 1974 until 1986, the <a href="/wiki/Seven_Network" title="Seven Network">Seven Network</a> and the <a href="/wiki/ABC_(Australian_TV_channel)" class="mw-redirect" title="ABC (Australian TV channel)">Australian Broadcasting Corporation</a> (ABC) were given exclusive rights to VFL/AFL games. The only year Seven did not telecast games was <a href="/wiki/1987_VFL_season" title="1987 VFL season">1987</a> when the rights were bought by Broadcom, which on-sold the rights to the ABC in Victoria. Seven regained the rights in <a href="/wiki/1988_VFL_season" title="1988 VFL season">1988</a> and also exclusive rights.
</p><p>With the launch of subscription television in Australia, AFL match coverage commenced on cable television. <a href="/wiki/Optus_Vision" class="mw-redirect" title="Optus Vision">Optus Vision</a> bid for and won exclusive pay-TV rights from 1996 to 2001, screening coverage on its own 24-hour AFL channel, branded <i>Sports AFL</i> in Brisbane, Sydney and Melbourne (where available). The Sports AFL channel was later closed due to financial issues and relaunched in March 1999 as <a href="/wiki/C7_Sport" title="C7 Sport">C7 Sport</a> by the <a href="/wiki/Seven_Network" title="Seven Network">Seven Network</a> with AFL match coverage also transferred to the new channel. C7 Sport became available in regional areas not in the <a href="/wiki/Foxtel" title="Foxtel">Foxtel</a> or <a href="/wiki/Optus_Vision" class="mw-redirect" title="Optus Vision">Optus Vision</a> licence area via <a href="/wiki/Austar" title="Austar">Austar</a> soon after the re-launch. The AFL coverage was not available through Foxtel at this time as the Seven Network and Foxtel disagreed on the cost of carrying the C7 channel. These issues regarding C7 and AFL broadcasting rights evolved into a court case between not just the Seven Network and <a href="/wiki/News_Limited" class="mw-redirect" title="News Limited">News Limited</a> but Seven against the owners of the Nine Network and Network Ten in the years that followed.
</p><p>On 25 January 2001, the Seven Network's main rivals, the <a href="/wiki/Kerry_Packer" title="Kerry Packer">Kerry Packer</a> led <a href="/wiki/Nine_Network" title="Nine Network">Nine Network</a>, <a href="/wiki/Network_Ten" class="mw-redirect" title="Network Ten">Network Ten</a> and pay-TV's <a href="/wiki/Foxtel" title="Foxtel">Foxtel</a> set up a consortium which bid $500&#160;million for the right to broadcast the <a href="/wiki/2002_AFL_season" title="2002 AFL season">2002</a>–<a href="/wiki/2006_AFL_season" title="2006 AFL season">2006 seasons</a> inclusive. Seven had purchased a guaranteed right to make the last bid in 1995,<sup id="cite_ref-SevenFox_99-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SevenFox-99"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>99<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> but decided not to outbid their rivals.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>100<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The games were split between the networks, with Nine screening <a href="/wiki/Friday_Night_Football_(AFL)" title="Friday Night Football (AFL)">Friday Night Football</a>, a live Sunday afternoon game in the east and, if needed, a doubleheader for WA and SA, Ten screened a Saturday afternoon and a Saturday night match, with the remaining three matches shown on Foxtel. Foxtel set up its own version of a dedicated AFL-only channel, the <a href="/wiki/Fox_Footy_Channel" title="Fox Footy Channel">Fox Footy Channel</a>, which showed every game on replay during the week, as well as many news, <a href="/wiki/Talk_radio" title="Talk radio">talkback</a> and general interest shows related to Australian rules football.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>101<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>When the rights were offered again in January 2006 for the <a href="/wiki/2007_AFL_season" title="2007 AFL season">2007</a> to 2011 seasons, Seven formed an alliance with Ten and used its guaranteed last bid rights to match Nine's offer of $780&#160;million to win back the broadcast rights in what was the biggest sport telecasting deal in Australian history at the time. After lengthy negotiations, Foxtel agreed to be a broadcast partner and showed four live matches each week, although no longer on a dedicated AFL channel.<sup id="cite_ref-SevenFox_99-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SevenFox-99"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>99<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Seven took back the Friday night match and only one game on Sunday, while Ten retained showing two matches on Saturdays. Foxtel showed two games on Saturday and two on Sunday, including a late afternoon or twilight game.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>102<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>The 2012–2016 rights were bought by Seven, Foxtel and Telstra for $1.25 billion, the biggest sport telecasting deal in Australian history at the time. As part of the deal, Foxtel would show all home-and-away AFL matches live, as well as all Finals bar the grand final, via the resurrected Fox Footy. Telstra would broadcast all matches via mobile and Seven would broadcast three live matches (Friday night, Saturday night and Sunday afternoon) and one delayed match (Saturday afternoon). Seven also had the option to on-sell one game a week to either Nine or Ten; this did not happen.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>103<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>104<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>The 2017–2022 rights were re-bought by Seven, Foxtel and Telstra for $2.5 billion, besting the previous deal to become the most lucrative in Australian history at the time. Under the terms of the deal, Seven broadcasts at least three live matches per round as well as all Finals matches, whilst Foxtel broadcasts (or simulcasts Seven's feed) all nine matches per round, as well as all Finals bar the grand final, which is exclusively broadcast by Seven. Telstra continues to maintain exclusive mobile broadcast rights to all matches.<sup id="cite_ref-CurrentTVrightsOverview_98-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CurrentTVrightsOverview-98"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>98<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> There are some variations in broadcasting dependent on the relevant <a href="/wiki/States_and_territories_of_Australia" title="States and territories of Australia">state or territory</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>105<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The agreement with Seven, Foxtel and Telstra was extended in 2020 by two years to include the 2023 and 2024 seasons.
</p><p>In 2021 Telstra's AFL streaming service, AFL Live Pass, was removed and replaced with access to <a href="/wiki/Kayo_Sports" title="Kayo Sports">Kayo</a>, run by <a href="/wiki/Hubbl" title="Hubbl">Hubbl</a> (then called Streamotion), a wholly owned subsidiary of Foxtel.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>106<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>The 2025–2031 rights were re-bought by Seven, Foxtel and Telstra for $4.5 billion, once again besting the previous deal to become the most lucrative in Australian history. As part of the deal, Seven would show three-and-a-half games a week on average during the home-and-away season, as well as all Finals and the Brownlow Medal. This includes Thursday Night games for the first 15 rounds of each season and streaming rights to all matches they broadcast via 7+. Fox Footy would continue to show every home-and-away game and every final live bar the Grand Final via Foxtel and Kayo, as well as select matches on Binge. All Foxtel matches will have Fox Footy commentary, including simulcasts of Channel Seven matches, and Saturday matches will be exclusive to Fox Footy for the first fifteen rounds bar any marquee matches. These arrangements differ outside of Victoria, where every local team's match will be broadcast on free-to-air, albeit with Saturday matches on delay for the first eight rounds.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>107<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>108<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>109<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="International_broadcasts">International broadcasts</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Australian_Football_League&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: International broadcasts"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="International_broadcast_history">International broadcast history</h4><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Australian_Football_League&amp;action=edit&amp;section=43" title="Edit section: International broadcast history"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>Historically AFL broadcasts in other countries have varied.
</p><p>In late 1979, the brand new <a href="/wiki/ESPN" title="ESPN">ESPN</a> cable network signed the league's first international TV contract. Coverage began with the 1980 season with matches airing on late Friday and Saturday nights, sometimes live but usually one or two week tape delayed to up to 2.5 million subscribers.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>110<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> At the time, reports indicated ESPN paid the VFL nearly $100,000 (the VFL's Australian TV rights deal at the time was just $600,000<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>111<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>). The 1983 VFL Grand Final was the first time in history that the Grand Final was broadcast live into the US.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>112<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Coverage continued on ESPN until 1986, when the sport was dropped after which it was not broadcast in the US for over a decade.
</p><p>New Zealand was the second country which held broadcast rights in 1980, with highlight packages with the Grand Final going live into the country.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>113<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In the early 1990s, American regional sports network <a href="/wiki/Prime_Sports" title="Prime Sports">Prime Sports</a> (unrelated to the <a href="/wiki/Prime7" title="Prime7">Australian regional television network</a>) aired Seven's weekly highlight show as well as the grand final. Some other English speaking countries have shown the game, however, it has been since 2008 that channels in other countries began televising matches. From 1998 to 2006 games were broadcast in the United States by the <a href="/wiki/Fox_Soccer" title="Fox Soccer">Fox Sports World</a> network.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>114<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In 2007, after the record domestic television rights deal, the AFL secured an additional bonus: greater international television rights and increase exposure to overseas markets, including a five-year deal with <a href="/wiki/Setanta_Sports" title="Setanta Sports">Setanta Sports</a> and new deals with other overseas <a href="/wiki/Pay-TV" class="mw-redirect" title="Pay-TV">pay-TV</a> networks. The deal ended early in 2009 when Setanta stopped broadcasting into Great Britain. ESPN again took up the contract.<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>115<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Additionally, AFL games can be shown in Irish pubs and sport pubs by request in <a href="/wiki/Bangkok" title="Bangkok">Bangkok</a> although <a href="/wiki/Thailand" title="Thailand">Thailand</a> has no AFL rights because these pubs have subscribed internet cable services.
</p>

<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Radio">Radio</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Australian_Football_League&amp;action=edit&amp;section=45" title="Edit section: Radio"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>The first broadcast of a VFL game was by <a href="/wiki/Radio_National" title="Radio National">3AR</a> in 1923, the year that licensed broadcasting commenced in Australia. The first commentator was <a href="/w/index.php?title=Wallace_Shallard&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Wallace Shallard (page does not exist)">Wallace (Jumbo) Shallard</a>, a former Geelong player who went on to have a long and respected career in print and broadcast media. The VFL/AFL has been broadcast every year since then by the ABC and (since 1927) by various commercial stations. The saturation period was the early 1960s when seven of the eight extant radio stations (<a href="/wiki/Radio_National" title="Radio National">3AR</a>, <a href="/wiki/3UZ" class="mw-redirect" title="3UZ">3UZ</a>, <a href="/wiki/3DB_(Melbourne)" title="3DB (Melbourne)">3DB</a>, <a href="/wiki/3KZ" class="mw-redirect" title="3KZ">3KZ</a>, <a href="/wiki/3AW" title="3AW">3AW</a>, <a href="/wiki/3XY" class="mw-redirect" title="3XY">3XY</a> and <a href="/wiki/3AK" title="3AK">3AK</a>) broadcast VFL games each week, as well as broadcasts of Geelong games by local station <a href="/wiki/K-Rock_(Australia)" class="mw-redirect" title="K-Rock (Australia)">3GL</a>. (At this time, the only alternative that radio listeners had to listen to the football on a Saturday afternoon were the classical music and fine arts programs that were broadcast by <a href="/wiki/3LO" class="mw-redirect" title="3LO">3LO</a>).
</p><p>The AFL's contracted radio broadcast partners are:
</p>
<ul><li>National:</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/ABC_Radio_Grandstand" title="ABC Radio Grandstand">ABC Sport</a> (broadcasts matches across Australia to selected major cities in ACT/NSW/QLD/SA/TAS/WA)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Triple_M_Adelaide" title="Triple M Adelaide">Triple M</a> <a href="/wiki/Adelaide" title="Adelaide">Adelaide</a> *</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Triple_M_Brisbane" title="Triple M Brisbane">Triple M</a> <a href="/wiki/Brisbane" title="Brisbane">Brisbane</a> *</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Triple_M_Hobart" title="Triple M Hobart">Triple M</a> <a href="/wiki/Hobart" title="Hobart">Hobart</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Triple_M_Melbourne" title="Triple M Melbourne">Triple M</a> <a href="/wiki/Melbourne" title="Melbourne">Melbourne</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Triple_M_Perth" title="Triple M Perth">Triple M</a> <a href="/wiki/Perth" title="Perth">Perth</a> *</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Triple_M_Sydney" title="Triple M Sydney">Triple M</a> <a href="/wiki/Sydney" title="Sydney">Sydney</a> *</li>
<li>Community &amp; Local:</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/SEN_SA" class="mw-redirect" title="SEN SA">SEN SA Radio</a> <a href="/wiki/Adelaide" title="Adelaide">Adelaide</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/FIVEaa" title="FIVEaa">FIVEAA Radio</a> <a href="/wiki/Adelaide" title="Adelaide">Adelaide</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/4AAA" class="mw-redirect" title="4AAA">98.9FM Radio</a> <a href="/wiki/Brisbane" title="Brisbane">Brisbane</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/K-Rock_(Australia)" class="mw-redirect" title="K-Rock (Australia)">K-Rock Radio</a> <a href="/wiki/Geelong" title="Geelong">Geelong</a> *</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/3AW" title="3AW">3AW Radio</a> <a href="/wiki/Melbourne" title="Melbourne">Melbourne</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/1116_SEN" title="1116 SEN">1116 SEN Radio</a> <a href="/wiki/Melbourne" title="Melbourne">Melbourne</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/6PR" title="6PR">6PR Radio</a> <a href="/wiki/Perth" title="Perth">Perth</a></li></ul>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Triple_M_Adelaide" title="Triple M Adelaide">Triple M</a> <a href="/wiki/Adelaide" title="Adelaide">Adelaide</a> (broadcasts only <a href="/wiki/Adelaide_Football_Club" title="Adelaide Football Club">Adelaide</a> and <a href="/wiki/Port_Adelaide_Football_Club" title="Port Adelaide Football Club">Port Adelaide</a> matches, including the <a href="/wiki/Showdown_(AFL)" title="Showdown (AFL)">Showdown</a>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Triple_M_Brisbane" title="Triple M Brisbane">Triple M</a> <a href="/wiki/Brisbane" title="Brisbane">Brisbane</a> (broadcasts only <a href="/wiki/Brisbane_Lions" title="Brisbane Lions">Brisbane</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gold_Coast_Suns" title="Gold Coast Suns">Gold Coast</a> matches, including the <a href="/wiki/QClash" title="QClash">QClash</a>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/K-Rock_(Australia)" class="mw-redirect" title="K-Rock (Australia)">K-Rock</a> <a href="/wiki/Geelong" title="Geelong">Geelong</a> (includes broadcasts of <a href="/wiki/Geelong_Football_Club" title="Geelong Football Club">Geelong</a> matches)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Triple_M_Perth" title="Triple M Perth">Triple M</a> <a href="/wiki/Perth" title="Perth">Perth</a> (broadcasts only <a href="/wiki/Fremantle_Football_Club" title="Fremantle Football Club">Fremantle</a> and <a href="/wiki/West_Coast_Eagles" title="West Coast Eagles">West Coast</a> matches, including the <a href="/wiki/Western_Derby" title="Western Derby">Western Derby</a>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Triple_M_Sydney" title="Triple M Sydney">Triple M</a> <a href="/wiki/Sydney" title="Sydney">Sydney</a> *(broadcasts only <a href="/wiki/Greater_Western_Sydney_Giants" title="Greater Western Sydney Giants">Greater Western Sydney</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sydney_Swans" title="Sydney Swans">Sydney</a> matches,, including the <a href="/wiki/Sydney_Derby_(AFL)" title="Sydney Derby (AFL)">Battle of Sydney</a>)</li></ul>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="Non-English_radio">Non-English radio</h4><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Australian_Football_League&amp;action=edit&amp;section=46" title="Edit section: Non-English radio"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>The vast majority of radio broadcasting is done in <a href="/wiki/Australian_English" title="Australian English">English</a>. However, ethnic radio stations broadcast the AFL in a variety of languages, including <a href="/wiki/Arabic_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Arabic language">Arabic</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chinese_language" title="Chinese language">Chinese</a>, <a href="/wiki/Greek_language" title="Greek language">Greek</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hindi" title="Hindi">Hindi</a> and <a href="/wiki/Spanish_language" title="Spanish language">Spanish</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>116<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Many also broadcast in <a href="/wiki/Australian_Aboriginal_languages" title="Australian Aboriginal languages">Indigenous languages</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-indlang_117-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-indlang-117"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>117<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> as the sport is very popular among Indigenous Australians.
</p>
<table class="wikitable sortable">
<tbody><tr>

<tr>
<td><a href="/wiki/Central_Australian_Aboriginal_Media_Association" title="Central Australian Aboriginal Media Association">Central Australian Aboriginal Media Association</a> (CAAMA)
</td>
<td><a href="/wiki/Arrernte_language" title="Arrernte language">Arrernte</a>
</td>

<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Internet">Internet</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Australian_Football_League&amp;action=edit&amp;section=47" title="Edit section: Internet"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>The AFL's contracted internet/mobile broadcast partner is <a href="/wiki/Telstra" title="Telstra">Telstra</a>. The AFL also provides exclusive broadband content, including streaming video for international fans, via its website. Telstra also hosts the websites of all the 18 AFL clubs.
</p><p>However, the website is frequently derided by users for its convoluted <a href="/wiki/Information_architecture" title="Information architecture">information architecture</a> and <a href="/wiki/Software_bloat" title="Software bloat">bloated</a> presentation.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>118<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>119<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Since 2012, Telstra has broadcast live matches over its <a href="/wiki/Telstra#Mobile_networks" title="Telstra">Next G</a> mobile network for a pay-per-view or season fee.<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>120<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Since 2019, <a href="/wiki/Kayo_Sports" title="Kayo Sports">Kayo</a> has broadcast every game, except the Grand Final, live. In Feb 2021, Telstra terminated the AFL Live Pass service, replacing it with access to Kayo at a discount for Telstra customers.
</p><p>Streaming rights outside of Australia for full games are currently held by the Watch AFL subscription service operated by Fox Sports Australia.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Corporate_relations">Corporate relations</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Australian_Football_League&amp;action=edit&amp;section=48" title="Edit section: Corporate relations"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Sponsorship">Sponsorship</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Australian_Football_League&amp;action=edit&amp;section=49" title="Edit section: Sponsorship"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>The VFL/AFL's competition naming sponsors have been:
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Carlton_%26_United_Breweries" title="Carlton &amp; United Breweries">Carlton &amp; United Breweries</a> (1980–81, 86, 89–94, 2001–03)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Holden" title="Holden">Holden</a> (1982–83)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Nissan" title="Nissan">Nissan</a> (1984–85)</li>
<li>Sportsplay (1987)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Elders_Limited" title="Elders Limited">Elders IXL</a> (1988)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Coca-Cola_Amatil" title="Coca-Cola Amatil">Coca-Cola</a> (1995–2000)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Toyota_Australia" title="Toyota Australia">Toyota</a> (2004–present)</li></ul>
<p>The AFL's contracted print media partner is <a href="/wiki/News_Corp_Australia" title="News Corp Australia">News Corp Australia</a>. The <i><a href="/wiki/AFL_Record" title="AFL Record">AFL Record</a></i> is a match-day magazine published by the AFL and is read by around 225,000 people each week.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Membership">Membership</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Australian_Football_League&amp;action=edit&amp;section=50" title="Edit section: Membership"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>The AFL sells memberships that entitle subscribers to reserve seats for matches at <a href="/wiki/Docklands_Stadium" title="Docklands Stadium">Docklands Stadium</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Melbourne_Cricket_Ground" title="Melbourne Cricket Ground">Melbourne Cricket Ground</a> in Melbourne. AFL members also receive priority access to finals. Three levels of memberships are offered, bronze, silver and full (gold). Only full members have guaranteed access to preliminary and grand final matches. Bronze members are restricted to fewer matches at the MCG only.<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>121<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Merchandising">Merchandising</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Australian_Football_League&amp;action=edit&amp;section=51" title="Edit section: Merchandising"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>The AFL runs a chain of stores that sell merchandise from all clubs. Merchandise is also available from other retailers.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="AFL_World">AFL World</h4><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Australian_Football_League&amp;action=edit&amp;section=52" title="Edit section: AFL World"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>A modern museum called the Hall of Fame and Sensation opened in Melbourne in 2003 to celebrate the culture of the AFL and to provide a venue for the <a href="/wiki/Australian_Football_Hall_of_Fame" title="Australian Football Hall of Fame">Australian Football Hall of Fame</a>. The museum, a licensed offshoot of the AFL, was originally touted for the MCG but the Hall of Fame failed to receive support from the Melbourne Cricket Club. The new QV shopping centre on Swanston Street was then chosen as the location. However, controversy followed the appointment of an administrator as the museum began running at a loss. Many blamed high entry prices, which were subsequently reduced and the museum remained open to the public. In early 2006 the name was changed to AFL World. It featured various honour boards and memorabilia as well as a range of innovative interactive displays designed to immerse visitors in the experience of elite Australian rules football. It was closed in 2008.
</p>
