<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="Gambling">Gambling</h4><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Australian_Football_League&amp;action=edit&amp;section=54" title="Edit section: Gambling"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>The AFL is the subject of footy tipping and betting competitions around Australia run by individuals, syndicates, workplaces and professional <a href="/wiki/Bookmaker" title="Bookmaker">bookmakers</a>. In recent years national website based tipping competitions have started to replace the traditional but more labour-intensive, office or pub run competitions.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Fantasy_football_(Australian_rules_football)" class="mw-redirect" title="Fantasy football (Australian rules football)">Fantasy football</a> competitions based on actual player statistics (number of kicks, marks, goals etc.) are also very popular on websites and in newspapers.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Activism">Activism</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Australian_Football_League&amp;action=edit&amp;section=55" title="Edit section: Activism"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="LGBTIQ_policy">LGBTIQ policy</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Australian_Football_League&amp;action=edit&amp;section=56" title="Edit section: LGBTIQ policy"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>The AFL has declared its support for <a href="/wiki/LGBT_community" class="mw-redirect" title="LGBT community">LGBTIQ</a> community, organising pride games in June 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>122<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In September 2017, in conjunction with the <a href="/wiki/Australian_Marriage_Law_Postal_Survey" title="Australian Marriage Law Postal Survey">Australian Marriage Law Postal Survey</a>, the AFL modified its logo sign at <a href="/wiki/Docklands_Stadium" title="Docklands Stadium">Docklands Stadium</a> support of <a href="/wiki/Same-sex_marriage_in_Australia" title="Same-sex marriage in Australia">same-sex marriage</a> (however, only for 24 hours).<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>123<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>124<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> However, As of 2023<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Australian_Football_League&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup> there has never been an openly <a href="/wiki/Category:LGBTQ_players_of_Australian_rules_football" title="Category:LGBTQ players of Australian rules football">gay AFL player</a>, past or present, making the AFL the only major professional sporting code in the world where this is the case.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_125-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-125"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>125<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> AFL CEO Gillon McLachlan has stated that "the pressure and the weight of being... the first AFL player who comes out and plays as an out, gay man" was too much of a burden for the known gay players in the league to come out.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_125-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-125"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>125<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The AFL has also stated that it will be "proud to stand shoulder to shoulder" with any player who comes out.<sup id="cite_ref-:2_126-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:2-126"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>126<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Former players and officials have suggested that a much stronger reasons for the lack of out gay players is a culture of homophobia and silence within the AFL, with former captain and ally <a href="/wiki/Robert_Murphy_(footballer)" title="Robert Murphy (footballer)">Bob Murphy</a> recalling shamefully his offhanded use of homophobic slurs as a young player.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_125-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-125"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>125<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Homophobic language remains a problem at games with legal recommendations from the Australian Sports Commission made in 2000 to address this still not implemented.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_125-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-125"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>125<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In 2015 the <a href="/wiki/Sydney_Swans" title="Sydney Swans">Sydney Swans</a> played a pre-season game at <a href="/wiki/Drummoyne_Oval" title="Drummoyne Oval">Drummoyne Oval</a> against <a href="/wiki/Fremantle_Dockers" class="mw-redirect" title="Fremantle Dockers">Fremantle Dockers</a> as a Pride Game. This became an annual event, which has grown from year to year in strength and support. The club has Sydney an official LGBTQIA+ supporter group, Rainbow Swans.<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>127<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In September 2017 the AFL ruled that <a href="/wiki/Hannah_Mouncey" title="Hannah Mouncey">Hannah Mouncey</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Transgender" title="Transgender">transgender</a> woman, <a href="/wiki/Transgender_people_in_sport" class="mw-redirect" title="Transgender people in sport">was ineligible</a> for selection in the 2018 <a href="/wiki/Women%27s_Australian_rules_football" title="Women&#39;s Australian rules football">AFLW</a> draft.<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>128<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> There has been some opposition to the AFL's decision.<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>129<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>130<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>It has been suggested that the men's game could do more to promote inclusivity, as has been done in the AFLW. The <a href="/wiki/Pride_Round_(AFLW)" class="mw-redirect" title="Pride Round (AFLW)">AFLW Pride Round</a> has been officially held since 2021, although there were individual AFLW clubs who had played Pride games since 2018. The intention of the Pride Round is to celebrate <a href="/wiki/Gender_diversity" title="Gender diversity">gender diversity</a>, promote inclusion for <a href="/wiki/LGBTIQA%2B" class="mw-redirect" title="LGBTIQA+">LGBTIQA+</a> players, and to help stamp out <a href="/wiki/Homophobia" title="Homophobia">homophobia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>131<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>132<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> All 18 clubs support the round.<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>133<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> As of November 2023<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Australian_Football_League&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup> the men's league had no plans to introduce a Pride Round in the men's game.<sup id="cite_ref-bourke2023_70-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bourke2023-70"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>70<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>134<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Voice_to_Parliament">Voice to Parliament</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Australian_Football_League&amp;action=edit&amp;section=57" title="Edit section: Voice to Parliament"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>The AFL supported the creation of an <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_Voice_to_Parliament" title="Indigenous Voice to Parliament">Indigenous Voice to Parliament</a>, ahead of the <a href="/wiki/2023_Australian_Indigenous_Voice_referendum" title="2023 Australian Indigenous Voice referendum">2023 Australian Indigenous Voice referendum</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>135<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Lawsuits">Lawsuits</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Australian_Football_League&amp;action=edit&amp;section=58" title="Edit section: Lawsuits"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>In 2023, a group of former players began a class-action lawsuit against the league regarding the concussions that they suffered while playing. The case is similar to the cases including cases against the <a href="/wiki/National_Football_League" title="National Football League">NFL</a> and the <a href="/wiki/National_Hockey_League" title="National Hockey League">NHL</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>136<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>137<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In 2023, former female umpire Libby Toovey took the league to the <a href="/wiki/Fair_Work_Commission" title="Fair Work Commission">Fair Work Commission</a>, claiming that she was dismissed after uncovering systemic abuse of female umpires by the league.<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>138<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
